1001 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Beal v. Benton County


No. W2013-01290-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 27


December 10, 2013, Session 
January 27, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Benton County. No. 2670. Don R. Ash, Senior Judge, by designation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a decision to deduct insurance premiums from some county employees' salaries, while providing the same insurance to other county employees with no salary deduction, violated equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in granting the county summary judgment because employees failed to meet their burden to set forth specific facts showing that the county commission's decision to treat them disparately was unreasonable or not rationally related to a legitimate government interest; [2]-The commission determined that a cap on the county's contribution to employee insurance benefits was needed to remedy a budget shortfall; [3]-The decision to cap benefits was rationally related to the legitimate legislative interest of balancing the budget.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed.

 

1002 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Donte N.


No. E2013-01617-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 19


November 7, 2013, Submitted on Briefs 
January 17, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. No. 129461. Timothy Irwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court erred in terminating a father's parental rights to three children on grounds of abandonment by willful failure to support, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-1-102(1)(A)(i) (2010) and 36-1-113(g)(1) (Supp. 2013), because there was no proof regarding the father's work history, income, or his ability to work during the applicable statutory period, and the trial court's findings regarding the issue of willful conduct were conclusory; [2]-Clear and convincing evidence supported terminating the father's rights on grounds of abandonment by exhibiting wanton disregard prior to incarceration, § 36-1-102(1)(A)(iv), because during the six-year period the children had been removed from his custody, the father repeatedly incurred criminal charges, some of which involved inappropriate sexual behavior with minors, and continued to incur criminal charges up to the time of trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; matter remanded.

Womble v. Univ. Health Sys.


No. E2012-02664-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 18; 37 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1159


September 17, 2013, Session 
January 16, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 1-347-11. Dale Workman, Judge.
Womble v. State, 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 440 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 3, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-9-112(a) was not an unconstitutional delegation of authority where it delegated the administrative responsibility for University of Tennessee Memorial Research Center and Hospital employees to the University Health System, Inc., not any legislative authority; [2]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-9-1301(b)(1) did not violate Tenn. Const. art. II, § 31, as the statute clearly did not extend the State's credit, the State assumed no obligation for any employee costs, and the statute promoted the public purpose of ensuring the maintenance and delivery of quality health care to a large geographical area of Tennessee.


OUTCOME: Ruling reversed.

In re Kierra B.


No. E2012-02539-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 15


December 6, 2013, Assigned on Briefs 
January 14, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed, in Part, and, Reversed, in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Sullivan County (Kingsport). No. J37321. Mark Toohey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed, in Part, and, Reversed, in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Clear and convincing evidence supported termination of a mother's parental rights as being in the best interest of two children, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(i) (Supp. 2013), because the mother, inter alia, had unresolved substance abuse and mental health issues, lacked safe and adequate housing, and made no efforts to establish a home or cure the reasons the children were removed; [2]-Clear and convincing evidence supported termination of a father's parental rights as being in his child's best interest, § 36-1-113(i), because, inter alia, the father failed to support the child, and the father was not a part of the child's life prior to incarceration and was unable to be a part of the child's life until released from jail, at which time he would have been absent from the child's life for twelve years.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded.

Mortgage Elec. Registration Sys. v. Ditto


No. E2012-02292-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 1


September 18, 2013, Session 
January 2, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Mortgage Elec. Registration Sys. v. Ditto, 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 880 (Tenn., Oct. 20, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 12-0058. Hon. W. Frank Brown, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because appellant was never given an independent interest in the property, and it did not suffer an injury by the sale of the property at issue, and the only injury suffered by appellant related to the future effect the case could have on its business model, which was not a distinct and palpable injury capable of being redressed by the court, the trial court's grant of the purchaser's motion for judgment on the pleadings was properly granted as appellant did not have standing to file suit to set aside the tax sale of the property for lack of notice under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2502(c) and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment; [2]-The failure to tender the appropriate funds when filing the petition to set aside the sale under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2504(c) was not a prerequisite for relief.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; case remanded.

Bevels v. Tubbs


No. W2012-02375-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 778


August 22, 2013, Session 
November 27, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Reversed in Part, Vacated in Part, and Remanded. An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-000049-10. James F. Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Reversed in Part, Vacated in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in holding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction on the ground that the tenants failed to comply with bond requirements set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-15-732(b) and (c)(1) (2009) where nothing in the record suggested that the amount of cash bond they paid was insufficient; [2]-Although the tenants had not cited to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 42.02 and 13.09 to the trial court or in their appellate brief, the reviewing court exercised its discretion to consider the rules; [3]-The trial court erred in dismissing the tenants' counterclaim and third-party complaint as null and void where Rules 42.02 and 13.09 gave the trial court the authority to separate the actions and retain jurisdiction over the counterclaim; [4]-A remand was appropriate to give the trial court the opportunity to exercise the discretion afforded it under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 42.02 and 13.09.


OUTCOME: Decision reversed; case remanded.

 

1008 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Shockley v. Mental Health Coop.


No. M2013-00494-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


429 S.W.3d 582; 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 726


September 25, 2013, Session 
November 4, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Shockley v. Mental Health Coop., Inc., 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 155 (Tenn., Feb. 11, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 12C2509. Hamilton V. Gayden, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-When plaintiff personal representative gave pre-suit notice, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-121, of her health care liability claim to an entity that, while related to the correct defendant health care provider, did not provide the health care in question, the notice was insufficient because the statute's requirements were strictly construed, and notice was not given to the entity that would be named as a defendant; [2]-Tenn. R. Civ. P. 15.03 did not let her retroactively amend the defective notice because it only applied to pleadings, and the notice was not a pleading, since it preceded the filing of a lawsuit; [3]-The suit had to be dismissed because the personal representative did not show extraordinary cause for failing to comply with the pre-suit notice requirement.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

McGarity v. Jerrolds


No. W2013-00250-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


429 S.W.3d 562; 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 552


July 17, 2013, Session 
August 27, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2014.
Appeal denied by McGarity v. Jerrolds, 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 160 (Tenn., Feb. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3. Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hardin County. No. CH-100. Ron E. Harmon, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Even with the stipulation that the paternal grandparents and the child had a significant existing relationship, the grandparents were required to show that the child was likely to suffer severe emotional harm due to the termination of that relationship in order for the trial court to grant the grandparents visitation; [2]-The grandparents failed to submit evidence to support a finding that the child was likely to suffer substantial harm or any other harm that could reasonably be categorized as severe, grave, distressing, or extreme; [3]-Without a showing of either substantial harm or severe emotional harm, the grandparents did not meet their burden to justify intrusion into the mother's and the adoptive-father's decision to terminate visitation, and the trial court erred in allowing grandparent visitation under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306(b)(1).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

Comm'rs v. Util. Mgmt. Review Bd.


No. M2012-01806-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


427 S.W.3d 375; 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 503


March 26, 2013, Session 
July 31, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Comm'rs of the Powell-Clinch Util. Dist. v. Util. Mgmt. Review Bd., 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 516 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 31, 2013)
Appeal denied by Util. Mgmt. Review Bd. v. Comm'rs of the Powell-Clinch Util. Dist., 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 907 (Tenn., Nov. 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part, Affirmed in Part, and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 111608-IV. Russell T. Perkins, Chancellor.
Comm'rs of the Powell-Clinch Util. Dist. v. Util. Mgmt. Review Bd., 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 347 (Tenn. Ct. App., May 24, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part, Affirmed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Application of the portion of the June 2009 amendments to Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-307(b)(2) (2005) permitting the removal of utility district commissioners (UDCs) for failing to fulfill their fiduciary responsibilities, absent the knowing or wilfulness elements, was an impermissible retrospective application of law under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20 since before the 2009 amendments to § 7-82-307(b), UDCs could be removed from office only upon a showing of knowing or willful misconduct; the amendments attached a new disability to past transactions by removing the elements of knowing and willfulness; [2]-Amended § 7-82-307(b) was not unconstitutionally vague since UDCs of ordinary intelligence could construe their fiduciary duty under Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-309(b)(1) (2011) when exercising the duties, powers, and authority set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. tit. 7, ch. 82.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, in part, and affirmed, in part. Matter remanded.

Johnston v. Swing


No. M2012-01760-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 476


April 12, 2013, Session 
July 26, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 081977-IV. Russell T. Perkins, Chancellor.
Walker v. Metro. Bd. of Parks & Rec., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 900 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 26, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether an attorney's due process rights were violated when he was prohibited from speaking on behalf of his former clients during two separate meetings of a metro department of parks and recreation board. HOLDINGS: [1]-The attorney's claim for the alleged deprivation of his rights under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 was not cognizable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; [2]-The attorney's claims related to the first board meeting were time-barred under Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-104(a)(3); [3]-The attorney's rights were not violated as to the second board meeting because he had actual notice of the board policy requiring fourteen days' notice before speaking well in advance of the second meeting; [4]-The attorney was not entitled to a declaratory judgment under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-103 because he failed to demonstrate that he was seeking to vindicate an existing right under then existing facts.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Womble v. State


No. E2012-01711-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 440


April 16, 2013, Session 
July 3, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Womble v. Univ. Health Sys., 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 18 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 16, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Tennessee Claims Commission for Eastern Division. No. T20120068. William O. Shults, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Tennessee Claims Commission had subject matter jurisdiction over the breach of contract and negligence claims of a nurse who was terminated from her employment, after the operation of a state university medical center where she worked was transferred to a private, non-profit corporation. HOLDINGS: [1]-The Commission did not have jurisdiction, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1) (Supp. 2012), to consider the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-9-112 (Supp. 2012), the statute which enabled the transfer of the medical center, the validity of the employee services agreement which the nurse signed, or to hear a claim arising from the alleged negligent deprivation of the nurse's property right in her position; [2]-The Commission did not have subject matter jurisdiction, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(L), over the nurse's third-party beneficiary claim.


OUTCOME: Order was affirmed, and the case was remanded.

Blackwell v. Haslam


No. M2012-01991-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 436


March 26, 2013, Session1


1 As discussed below, after oral argument in this cause, the parties were asked to submit supplemental briefs on the effect of an amendment to a pertinent Tennessee statute that was enacted after oral argument. The Court considered the appeal after the supplemental briefing was completed on June 18, 2013.

 
June 28, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2014.
As Corrected June 28, 2013
Appeal denied by Blackwell v. Haslam, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 854 (Tenn., Oct. 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Vacated in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 10-0739-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
Blackwell v. Haslam, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 23 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 11, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is Vacated in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in entering a judgment on the pleadings declaring that petitioner, whose Georgia pardon of his drug felonies expressly restored his right to possess a firearm, was entitled to possess firearms in Tennessee despite the prohibition of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1307(b)(1)(B); as Tennessee's public policy proscribed the restoration of firearm rights for persons convicted of a felony involving violence or a deadly weapon, which conflicted with Georgia's public policy, it would not be proper to grant the Georgia pardon full faith and credit if petitioner's crimes involved violence or firearms. As the record did not show the nature of his crimes, remand was required; [2]-As petitioner did not establish that he was deprived of a personal constitutional right cognizable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, he was not entitled to attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of judgment on the pleadings was vacated, its award of attorneys' fees to petitioner was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Aina-Labinjo v. Metro. Nashville Bd. of Pub. Educ.


No. M2012-01176-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 377


February 20, 2013, Session 
June 6, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 12587III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The chancery court had jurisdiction under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 16-11-102(a) and 29-25-101 to issue a writ of mandamus; [2]-However, it erred in issuing a writ of mandamus compelling a board of education to hear an appeal of the termination of a non-teaching employee; [3]-There was no testimony or other evidence introduced as to what, if any, policy the board had developed with respect to the dismissal of employees as required by the Education Improvement Act of 1991, Tenn. Code Ann.§ 49-2-301(b)(1)(FF); [4]-A declaratory judgment proceeding pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 et seq., was the more appropriate procedure; [5]-The employee petitioned for a writ of mandamus and, in the alternative, requested a declaration of her rights under the Charter of the Metropolitan Government of Nashville, Tennessee ,and the board's answer denied salient allegations of the petition.


OUTCOME: Order reversed an, peremptory writ of mandamus vacated, and case remanded.

State ex rel. Moncier v. Jones

2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 379


April 10, 2013, Session 
June 6, 2013, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 12C502. Hamilton V. Gayden, Jr., Judge.
United States v. Vassar, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7878 (E.D. Tenn., Jan. 6, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Disciplinary Counsel had immunity under Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9, § 27.1 in a suit filed by a disciplined attorney as the complaints' allegations concerned actions taken by Counsel in the performance of her duties during the disciplinary proceeding against the attorney, and the complaints did not allege conduct that was outside the scope of Counsel's employment; [2]-A trial court could not entertain a challenge to the constitutionality of Rule 9, § 27.1, even in a declaratory judgment action; [3]-The denial of the attorney's request for a declaration of his rights in connection with the effects of filling his claim against the State with the Tennessee Claims Commission was not arbitrary as the attorney sought an advisory opinion and it was not clear that such an opinion would have terminated the controversy.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Arnold v. Kennedy


No. M2011-02480-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 369


April 16, 2013, Assigned On Briefs 
May 31, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 11C-2862. D.J. Alissandratos, Chancellor Sitting by Designation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a parent was entitled to damages against a state court judge for the judge's alleged wrongful refusal to grant the parent's petition for a writ of habeas corpus regarding the appointment of a conservator for the parent's adult child. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court acted within its authority because the Supreme Court of Tennessee appointed a retired chancellor to hear the conservatorship proceeding under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 16-3-502(3)(A) and 17-2-109(a)(2); [2]-The probate court had jurisdiction pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 34-3-101; [3]-The parent's adult child was developmentally disabled under Tenn. Code Ann. § 34-1-101 (2007) because she suffered from Down syndrome; [4]-The judge's failure to act immediately upon the petition did not constitute a wrongful and willful failure to grant the writ so as to subject him to a suit for damages under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-108.


OUTCOME: Judgment of dismissal of the writ was affirmed, and the case was remanded for enforcement of the judgment.

Comm'rs of the Powell-Clinch Util. Dist. v. Util. Mgmt. Review Bd.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether 2009 amendments to Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-307(b)(2) (2005), which added failing to fulfill a commissioner's or commissioners' fiduciary responsibility in the operation or oversight of a utility district as a ground for the removal of a commissioner from a utility district, was to be applied retrospectively to remove utility district commissioners from office for acts allegedly committed prior to the effective date of the amendment. HOLDINGS: [1]-Application of the portion of the 2009 amendments to Tenn. 1019 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. Shelby County


No. W2012-01498-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 333


February 19, 2013, Session 
May 16, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in part, Vacated in part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-04-0860-2. Donald P. Harris, Senior Judge.
Bailey v. Shelby County, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44089 (W.D. Tenn., Mar. 17, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in part, Vacated in part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Former part-time employees for a county claimed that they were wrongfully excluded from the county's retirement plan. The employees' declaratory judgment action and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims were time-barred by Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-109 because the issue in the case was whether the county wrongfully refused to permit them to participate in the pension system, not whether the county defaulted on contractual installment payments, and their causes of action accrued when they discovered their injury -- that they were not included in the county retirement system.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Applicants' suit for declaratory judgment concerning department's denial of billboard permits was properly dismissed because applicants failed to petition department for a declaratory order under the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act (UAPA), Tenn. DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The Tennessee Board of Medical Examiners challenged a judgment reversing its decision that a physician convicted of driving under the influence (DUI) engaged in unprofessional, dishonorable, or unethical conduct as proscribed by Tenn. Littlefield v. Hamilton County Election Comm'n


No. E2012-00489-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 628


August 29, 2012, Session 
September 12, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in part and Reversed in part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 11C1520. Hon. W. Jeffery Hollingsworth, Judge.
Littlefield v. Hamilton County Election Comm'n, 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 602 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 3, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in part and Reversed in part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A declaratory judgment finding that Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-5-151(d) controlled the number of signatures needed for a recall of a mayor was reversed. The 2002 City Charter restatement was sufficient to enact a contrary charter provision under § 2-5-151(j), which allowed a contrary charter provision of a municipality with respect only to the statutory minimum number of signatures required in a petition. The minimum signature requirement contained in Chattanooga, Tenn., City Charter § 3.18 governed the minimum number of signatures required for a recall petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the findings that the referendum vote of August 1, 2002, did not effectively enact § 3.18 and that § 2-5-151(d) governed the requisite number of signatures required to support a recall petition. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed. The cause was remanded.

OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged an order dismissing for lack of jurisdiction their action seeking the return of seized property. The trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider appellants' arguments because it was a civil matter under the jurisdiction of the Department of Safety. The provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-201 et seq. were civil, not criminal, in nature and were not to be addressed in a criminal forum. Tenn. R. Crim. P. 41(g) did not provide the trial court with subject matter jurisdiction. Rule 41 essentially addressed search warrants, a situation not presented in the case.


OUTCOME: Ruling affirmed.

 

1043 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Tenn. Dep't of Safety ex rel. Harmon v. Bryant


No. E2011-01295-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 559


May 22, 2012, Session 
August 14, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Tenn. Dep't of Safety ex rel. Harmon v. Bryant, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 224 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 96819. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellants, owners of seized property, sought, in criminal court, to enforce subpoenas issued in an administrative asset forfeiture case. Dismissal was required because (1) Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-311(b) only let agencies seek to enforce such subpoenas, and (2) a criminal court had no jurisdiction to hear administrative discovery disputes. The statute did not violate due process because (1) courts only reviewed final agency orders, not administrative discovery disputes, and (2) Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-322(b)(1)(A) let the owners appeal a final order to the Davidson County, Tenn., Chancery Court.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Two towns passed ordinances under which a city and its utility were granted the right to provide gas to consumers. OVERVIEW: Billboards were erected prior to a town's prohibition of them. A town board of zoning appeals (BZA) affirmed the town's denial of plaintiff's request to reconstruct them. December 13, 2011, Session 
January 27, 2012, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 09-587-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Taxpayer's connections with Tennessee constituted a substantial nexus such that Tennessee's assessment of sales and use taxes against it were consistent with the Commerce Clause. The taxpayer was not a vendor whose only connection with customers in Tennessee in by common carrier or by mail. The taxpayer had created a de facto marketing and distribution mechanism within Tennessee's schools, and utilized Tennessee teachers to sell books to school children and their parents. Tennessee's school facilities and teachers were, in large part, funded by taxpayer dollars.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In-state bottled soft drink manufacturer bore the bottler's tax burden under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-402(b), and was not entitled to utilize an in-state distributor's franchise and excise tax credit because § 67-4-402(b) did not permit the distributor to pay the bottler's tax when it imported from an in-state manufacturer. Further, the statute's flexibility with regard to out-of-state and in-state manufacturers had some relevance to its objective of avoiding double taxation. Thus, it did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of U.S Const. amend. XIV or Tenn. Const. arts. I, § 8 and XI, § 8.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A judgment upholding a forfeiture of petitioner's property was affirmed. The seizing officers did not obtain the forfeiture warrants within five working days, but instead obtained extension orders under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-33-204(c)(2). The language in § 40-33-204(c)(2) was ambiguous on whether the extension order had to be obtained within five working days after the seizure of the property. In the absence of argument or authority that the extension order had to be obtained within five working days, the appellate court declined to interpret § 40-33-204(c)(2) to include such a requirement.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court is affirmed.

Whitmore v. Shelby County Gov't


No. W2010-01890-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 445


July 20, 2011, Session 
August 15, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-003608-09. Karen R. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A former employee's causes of action against a county under the Tennessee Human Rights Act (THRA) were time-barred. The general saving statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-1-105 (2000), did not "save" a claim non-suited and re-filed against a State entity under the THRA. The employee did not file her second complaint within the applicable limitations period and, as a result, lost the right to bring her action. Absent an express, clear, and unmistakable intent to the contrary, the saving statute could not be used to extend the period within which to file suit against the county under the THRA.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Hendricks v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole

2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 276


April 21, 2011, Assigned on Briefs 
May 25, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hendricks v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 904 (Tenn., Sept. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 09-548-I. Claudia C. Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Tennessee Board of Probation and Parole (Board) denied him parole, petitioner sought certiorari review alleging that the Board acted arbitrarily and illegally in denying him parole. After granting the writ and reviewing the record, the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) concluded that the Board acted lawfully, and dismissed the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that there was no evidence to support the Tennessee Board of Probation and Parole's (Board) decision to deny parole based on the seriousness of the offense, and therefore, he was denied due process. The court of appeals disagreed and found this argument utterly devoid of merit. The Board must consider the seriousness of the offense when making its decision in order to comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-503, and the denial of parole on the basis of this factor does not raise any constitutional issues and the appellate court will not review the intrinsic correctness of the Board's decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stewart v. Ray


No. M2010-01808-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 264


April 19, 2011, Assigned on Briefs 
May 19, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Stewart v. Ray, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 891 (Tenn., Sept. 26, 2011)
Reversed by Stewart v. Derrick, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 376 (Tenn., May 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 10-457-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prisoner filed a petition for certiorari naming as respondents the Commissioner of the Department of Correction and others (TDOC) allegedly responsible for determining his eligibility for parole. He alleged TDOC was incorrectly calculating his eligibility for parole. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granted TDOC's motion to dismiss for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. Prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prisoner argued, inter alia, that trial court erred in dismissing his case for failure to exhaust his administrative remedies. The court of appeals agreed. Any written request which made the agency aware of the substance of the controversy and asked the agency to act in accordance with a suggested course of action was sufficient. Prisoner's request for appeal to TDOC clearly raised the issue of whether the TDOC was calculating his sentence and his eligibility for parole in contravention of Howell v. State. Further, it asked TDOC to act in accordance with Howell and to not base eligibility for parole on his aggregate sentence. TDOC denied prisoner's request and told him that the decision was final and that there was no further avenue of appeal. The request for appeal on the basis of Howell and the letter denying appeal satisfied the requirement of requesting a declaratory order from the agency prior to filing what the trial court treated as a declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was remanded.

 

1078 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Creative Label, Inc. v. Tuck


No. W2010-01557-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 238


March 22, 2011, Session 
May 11, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Creative Label, Inc. v. Tuck, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 954 (Tenn., Sept. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Madison County. No. 59385. James F. Butler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Madison County (Tennessee) affirmed the determination of appellee State Board of Equalization that appellant taxpayer's leasehold interest in tax-exempt property belonging to an Industrial Development Board (IDB) of appellee city was not exempt from ad valorem taxation where the parties had executed a payment in lieu of taxes agreement under Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-53-305 (1993 & 1998). The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a corporation that operated property leased from the IDB. The taxpayer entered into an agreement with the city and appellee county that provided for payments in lieu of taxes (PILs). The taxpayer challenged the county's determination that its leasehold interest was not exempt from taxation. The court stated that the dispositive issue was whether § 7-53-305 permitted PILs of any amount by a taxpayer not within the enumerated categories to be made in lieu of all ad valorem taxes on the taxpayer's leasehold interest. Section 305(b), as it existed during the relevant period, was ambiguous with respect to which it provided relief from ad valorem taxation of leasehold interests. In light of the ambiguity, the court examined the purpose of the act establishing industrial development corporations. The court found nothing to suggest that the legislature intended a blanket exemption from taxation upon payment of a minimal PIL. The taxpayer's PILs served to reduce the taxable value of the taxpayer's leasehold interest, but did not entirely exempt the taxpayer from ad valorem taxes on its leasehold interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Doe v. Gwyn


No. E2010-01234-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 171


December 13, 2010, Session 
April 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Doe v. Gwyn, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 785 (Tenn., Aug. 24, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 10-0320. Hon. W. Frank Brown, III., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sex offender brought an action against the defendant Director of the Tennessee Bureau of Investigation and others (TBI) seeking a declaration that the Tennessee Sexual Offender and Violent Sexual Offender Registration, Verification and Tracking Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-39-201 et seq, was unconstitutional as applied to him. The Chancery Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) granted TBI's motion to dismiss. Sex offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: Sex offender argued, inter alia, that he should not be required to register under the Tennessee Sexual Offender and Violent Sexual Offender Registration, Verification and Tracking Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-39-201 et seq, (Act) because his criminal convictions occurred in other states prior to the passage of the Act, and the requirements of Act, as applied, violated his rights under the prohibition of ex post facto laws under Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 11. The court of appeals disagreed. The Act was enacted to protect the welfare of the people of Tennessee and not to further punish the offenders. There was a clear and rational non-punitive interest in the State of Tennessee's desire to inform the public of sex offender's history of sexual offenses. The registration requirement of the Act was not excessive with respect to its non-punitive purpose. And, sex offender did not state any reasons why requiring him to register would be more excessive than for any of the other thousands of sexual offenders.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1081 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Miltier v. Bank of Am., N.A.


No. E2010-00537-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 152


March 9, 2011, Session 
March 30, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Summary judgment granted by, Dismissed by Miltier v. Holly & Holly, PLLC, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 83350 (E.D. Tenn., June 12, 2013)
Costs and fees proceeding at, Remanded by Miltier v. Bank of Am., N.A., 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 419 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 26, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carter County. No. C9814 Thomas J. Seeley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his complaint for a wrongful foreclosure action against appellee lender, appellant debtor sought $ 200,000 in compensatory damages and $ 10 million in punitive damages. A jury awarded him $ 750,000 in compensatory damages and $ 300,000 in punitive damages. The Circuit Court for Carter County, Tennessee, reduced his compensatory damage award to $ 200,000 and affirmed the punitive damage award. The debtor sought review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reduced the debtor's compensatory damages in accordance with Tenn. R. Civ. P. 15.02 as he was limited to the damages that he pled. The court found that the debtor waived his challenge to the constitutionality of Rule 15.02. He failed to notify the attorney general of his challenge, and he did not raise the issue before the trial court. The debtor did not file a motion to amend the amount he demanded in his complaint. He argued that the issue of damages over $ 200,000 was tried by express or implied consent. The court was unpersuaded as the language of Rule 15.02 allowing amendment by consent did not allow the debtor to avoid the specific prohibition in Rule 15.02 against amendment after the verdict so as to increase the amount sued for in the action. Further, the court found that the specific prohibition in Rule 15.02 was not subject to waiver. Thus, the lender's introduction of a settlement offer it made to the debtor was not a waiver and an implied agreement to the amendment of the amount demanded. The trial court did not err in reducing the compensatory damages award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

1083 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Demitrus M. T.


No. E2009-02349-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 126


January 31, 2011, Session 
March 14, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Tennessee Claims Commission. No. 20050569. William O. Shults, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision of the Tennessee Claims Commission, which awarded a judgment in favor of appellees, the State of Tennessee, the Tennessee Department of Child Services (DCS), and employees of the State. The parents had set forth the wrongful death action by alleging that the State negligently caused the drowning of their six-month old infant while in the care of a placement caretaker.


OVERVIEW: The wrongful death action was filed in the Commission by the parents of the infant after he drowned in a bathtub while in the care of a friend of the family identified in a DCS safety plan as the placement caretaker. The friend left the infant unattended in the bathtub while she was otherwise occupied in an adjacent room. The issues were whether the infant was in the care, custody and control of the DCS so as to provide jurisdiction to the Commission; whether the DCS's case recordings, some of which were made more than a month after the event they purported to record, were inadmissible hearsay; and whether it was foreseeable to the DCS that the friend would leave the helpless infant unattended in a bathtub and let him drown. The court determined that the Commission properly found that it had jurisdiction because the DCS had control of the infant even though it did not have custody. However, the court held that the Commission erred in admitting one case recording that was completed over a month after the event that it was purported to record. Additionally, the Commission erred in finding that the infant's drowning and death was not foreseeable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Commission was affirmed with regard to the determination that it had subject matter jurisdiction and the admission of all but one of the case recordings. The decision was overruled with regard to an inadmissible case recording and the holding that the State could not be liable because the death of the infant was not foreseeable is vacated. The case was remanded.

Steppach v. Thomas


No. W2010-00606-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


346 S.W.3d 488; 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 91


November 16, 2010, Session 
February 28, 2011, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Steppach v. Thomas, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 766 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 17, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The City of Memphis did not violate its own procedures, Memphis, Tenn., Code of Ordinances, app. B, § 602, in granting an application for a planned development and a street closure. Section 602.2(A) contemplated that the application to close a street could be considered by the City Council even when an abutting landowner refused to sign the application. The phrases "abutting property owners" and "property owners with frontage" were construed as synonymous. Subdivision regulations discouraged through traffic on local roads and residents were concerted regarding the volume of existing through traffic.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Alcoa, Inc. v. Tenn. State Bd. of Equalization


No. E2010-00001-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 75


November 9, 2010, Session 
February 18, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Blount County. No. 08-142. Hon. Telford E. Forgety, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged appellee board of equalization's decision that upheld appellee county property tax assessor's levy of ad valorem taxes on certain raw materials the taxpayer used to fabricate sheets of aluminum at its manufacturing facility. The Chancery Court for Blount County, Tennessee, upheld the assessment. The taxpayer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued the raw materials were exempt from such taxation under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 28 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-216(a) as they were direct products of the soil in the hands of the producer or his immediate vendee. The court disagreed, finding that the raw materials underwent processing at least as extensive, and usually more extensive, than that of milling wheat into flour. The transformation of the product of the soil to the raw materials included changes in name, appearance, and consistency. The raw materials were not products of the soil entitled to the exemption under § 28. The taxpayer then argued that it was exempt as the raw materials were manufactured from the produce of Tennessee or any other state under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 30 and § 67-5-216(a). The raw materials were not articles manufactured by the taxpayer itself. The trial court did not err in refusing to pierce the corporate veil and find that the taxpayer was in fact the manufacturer of materials produced by its Texas subsidiary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the cause.

Boyce v. Tenn. Peace Officer Stds. & Training Comm'n


No. M2010-00211-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


354 S.W.3d 737; 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 55


October 15, 2010, Session 
February 10, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Boyce v. Tenn. Peace Officers Stds. & Training Comm'n, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 568 (Tenn., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 09-296-IV. Russell T. Perkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellee sheriff said Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-8-102(a)(9)(A), requiring his certification by the Tennessee Peace Officer Standards and Training Commission (POST), unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority. The statute was not unconstitutional because POST required discretionary authority as to subjects requiring flexibility and expertise to keep up with changing public safety needs, given (1) its authority to adopt and enforce rules needed to carry out the provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. tit. 38, ch. 8, and (2) a policy to train peace officers consistent with current professional standards.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to affirm an agency decision.

 

1087 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Destiny H. A. A. M. M.


No. E2010-01367-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 27


November 18, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
January 27, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court. Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for McMinn County. Nos. 26924-J & 27309-J. James F. Watson, Judge.
In re Gracie H., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 97 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 5, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed from a judgment of the Juvenile Court for McMinn County, Tennessee, which terminated the parental rights of the mother to her daughters.


OVERVIEW: The instant court found that there was abundant evidence of the mother's mental incompetence. The mother was diagnosed with bipolar disorder with psychotic features, schizoaffective disorder, delusional disorder, and borderline personality disorder. Additionally, the mother had at least three in-patient psychiatric hospitalizations, and had been treated for years with counseling and medication. Accordingly, clear and convincing evidence showed that the mother was mentally incompetent to parent her children and was likely to remain incompetent for the foreseeable future. Thus, the trial court properly terminated her parental rights on this basis. Next, the instant court found that a number of the best interest factors weighed against the mother. The instant court reasoned that the mother failed to effect a lasting adjustment after years of services by various social services agencies. Additionally, the mother allowed numerous individuals who presented a threat to her children to reside with her, her house was overrun with cockroaches, at times her utilities were shut off, and she remained delusional and mentally incompetent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1088 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Shelby County Health Care Corp. v. Baumgartner


No. W2008-01771-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 24


July 21, 2009, Session 1


1 As explained further herein, this appeal was held in abeyance pending the Tennessee Supreme Court's decision in another case involving similar issues.

 
January 26, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded. An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-002323-04. Kay S. Robilio, Judge.
Shelby County Health Care Corp. v. Nationwide Mut. Ins. Co., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 57 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 6, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A hospital did not have a duty under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-22-102 to conduct an inquiry into the identity of potential third-party tortfeasors to perfect its hospital lien. Construing Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-22-101(b) in pari materia with Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-22-104(b)(1), the hospital should have recovered only damages that were attributable to impairment of its lien by insurers, in light of the fact that, had the hospital's lien been honored, it would have received only one-third of the amounts paid to the patients. Section 29-22-104(b)(1) did not preclude inclusion of consequential damages.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

1089 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hopkins v. Bradley County


No. E2010-00832-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


338 S.W.3d 529; 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 724


October 4, 2010, Session 
November 19, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hopkins v. Bradley County, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 369 (Tenn., Apr. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9, Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bradley County. No. V-97-965. Hon. Jeri S. Bryant, Judge by Interchange.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee filed an action against defendants, a county, a sheriff's department, and officers, for denying him liberty without due process of law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The Circuit Court for Bradley County, Tennessee, entered partial summary judgment for the arrestee, finding that defendants violated Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-150, and it amounted to a constitutional violation. The court granted an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee presented himself to the sheriff's department pursuant to an arrest warrant, which provided for his release from jail on bond. He was able and willing to post the bond, but he was informed that because the allegations against him involved domestic violence, the department was required to hold him in custody for 12 hours after his arrest before he could post bond. Upon review, the court found that before an arrestee could be held for 12 hours under § 40-11-150(h), a magistrate had to find that he was a threat to a victim, public safety, or a bail risk under § 40-11-150(a). As there was no such finding in the arrestee's case, § 40-11-150(h) had not been triggered, and the court affirmed the finding that defendants violated the statute. However, the court found that the arrestee's constitutional rights to due process were not violated by defendants' mistake as to the meaning of § 40-11-150(h). The fact that he was held for 12 hours before being released on bail did not automatically constitute a constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that defendants violated § 40-11-150. The court reversed the trial court's finding that the violation of the statute deprived the arrestee of his due process rights. The court remanded the case to the trial court.

 

1090 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Valenti Mid-South Mgmt., LLC v. Farr


No. M2010-00313-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 715


September 8, 2010, Session 
November 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Valenti Mid-South Mgmt. v. Farr, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 414 (Tenn., Apr. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 08-1978-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) upholding an assessment of the taxpayer's franchise tax liability by defendant Tennessee Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, which operated a chain of restaurants in Tennessee, contested additional franchise taxes assessed on the value of land and buildings that it leased from a company commonly owned with the taxpayer. That company already had paid franchise taxes. The court held that the taxpayer and the company were not affiliated within the meaning of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2004(2) due to ownership of the taxpayer and the affiliated company by the same natural individuals. Those individuals could not qualify as "persons" that could be affiliated under the franchise tax law because Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2004(34) defined "person" or "taxpayer" to include business entities but not natural individuals. The companies were not being subjected to impermissible double taxation because the franchise tax was paid for the privilege of doing business in Tennessee and both companies were doing business in Tennessee. Because the companies were not affiliated, the taxpayer had no standing to argue that affiliated companies with negative net worth such as the taxpayer were treated differently than companies with positive net worth that could be assessed franchise taxes based on net worth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the chancery court.

Crawford v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr. & Quentin White


No. M2009-00439-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 587


June 8, 2010, Submitted on Briefs 
September 21, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Crawford v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr., 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 155 (Tenn., Feb. 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-2148-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner filed a declaratory judgment action to challenge respondent department of correction's denial of his request for a parole hearing. When no action was taken after the department's answer and the petitioner failed to set a date for a final hearing, the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed the complaint without prejudice and denied the petitioner's subsequent summary judgment motion. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted in 1975 and 1976 of eight felonies, including armed robbery with a deadly weapon, assault with intent to commit murder, and second degree murder. He received a life sentence for second degree murder, consecutive with his other sentences, In June 1978, the petitioner was released on extended furlough which required him to report regularly to his parole counselor and to obtain permission before leaving the state. The petitioner moved to California without permission and committed other crimes. After the petitioner's return to Tennessee prisons in 1985, he repeatedly requested parole hearings on his life sentence. His requests were denied on the basis that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-123(b)(1) prevented parole after violation of a conditional release. The petitioner alleged that the statute applied only to his armed robbery convictions. The trial court properly found that, because the summary judgment motion was filed over a year after entry of the final order dismissing the complaint, it did not have subject matter jurisdiction to consider the petitioner's summary judgment motion. The dismissal order was plainly a final judgment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1093 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Clear Channel Outdoors v. Tenn. DOT


No. M2009-01631-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


337 S.W.3d 801; 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 574


May 13, 2010, Session 
September 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Clear Channel Outdoors v. Tenn. DOT, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 165 (Tenn., Feb. 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-1839-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.
Clear Channel Outdoors v. Tenn. DOT, 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 78 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 13, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellants owners' grandfathered billboard was destroyed, appellee department authorized the owners to rebuild the billboard using like materials pursuant to Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1680-2-3-.04(2). The department filed a notice of charges stating the new billboard failed to comply with the regulation because it was not rebuilt with like materials. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) agreed. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended on appeal that the billboard was in compliance with the regulation and that the subsequent removal of the billboard constituted an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation. The court held that the administrative interpretation controlled unless it was plainly erroneous or inconsistent with the regulation itself. Therefore, courts gave great deference and controlling weight to an agency's interpretation of its own rules. Here, the owners used a steel post to rebuild the billboard in place of the original wooden one, and to allow a steel pole to replace a thirty-year-old wooden post was contrary to the stated purpose of the Federal Highway Beautification Act, 23 U.S.C.S. § 131, the Billboard Regulation and Control Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 54-21-101 et seq., and both the federal and state regulatory schemes. Accordingly, in light of the fact that an agency's interpretation of its regulations was given great deference, the board's commissioner's interpretation of "like materials" was reasonable and not in excess of his statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1094 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Watson v. Waters


No. E2009-01753-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 535


May 20, 2010, Session 
August 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State ex rel. Watson v. Waters, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 211 (Tenn., Mar. 9, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Tennessee ex rel. Watson v. Waters, 132 S. Ct. 576, 181 L. Ed. 2d 421, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8187 (U.S., 2011)
Related proceeding at Watson v. Waters, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 127 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Sevier County. Nos. 08-8-295, 08-9-368. David R. Duggan, 1 Judge.


1 Fifth Judicial District Circuit Court Judge sitting by interchange.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens brought various quo warranto actions against defendants, a county, the county Board, and the county major, in the Chancery Court for Sevier County (Tennessee). The trial court granted the defendants' Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6) motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that the county mayor improperly rescheduled a county Board meeting. The defendants filed motions to dismiss pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6), or in the alternative, motions for summary judgment. The trial court properly granted the motion to dismiss because the plaintiffs did not have standing for a private right of action. The plaintiffs did not allege a special interest or injury that resulted from the alleged actions of the defendants. The trial court found that in the nature of a quo warranto, the plaintiffs failed to establish any injury in fact caused by the actions of the defendants, and thus, lacked standing. The trial court properly rejected the plaintiffs arguments that quo warranto cases brought pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-35-110, without the consent of the district attorney general, did not require a special interest or injury for standing. The plaintiffs failed to show a distinct and palpable injury. Without finding that the plaintiffs had established any injury at all, even if there was any such injury, it would be an injury only to an interest that the plaintiffs shared in common with all other citizens.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs on appeal were assessed to the plaintiffs, The case was remanded to the trial court for the collection of costs assessed below.

 

1095 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Stoneybrook Golf Course, LLC v. City of Columbia


No. M2009-01780-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 473


June 7, 2010, Session 
July 26, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Maury County. No. 08-412. Robert L. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before buying land, appellant corporation received appellee city's assurance for support of the land's annexation and rezoning. When the city refused to go forward with the annexation and rezoning until a comprehensive land use plan was completed, the corporation sued the city asserting that the refusal constituted an unconstitutional moratorium. The Chancery Court for Maury County (Tennessee) dismissed the complaint. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation asserted that the trial court erred in granting the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court held a municipality could properly refuse a building permit for a land use in a newly annexed area when such use was repugnant to a pending and later enacted zoning ordinance. Further, resolutions or ordinances of the type here considered were referred to in cases from other jurisdictions as "stopgap" ordinances, "interim" ordinances, and as "emergency" ordinances because of their function and purpose to preserve temporarily the status quo of the municipality or section thereof to which they apply until a pending permanent zoning regulation could be finally adopted. Here, the corporation was the party asking to change the status quo. Without the concurrence of the city the corporation had only the right to build one residential unit per acre. All the city did was not accept the proposed change until it could study it carefully in light of detailed standards. Thus, the city did not violate corporation's rights by refusing to evaluate the corporation's request for rezoning until it could evaluate that request in light of a comprehensive plan.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Murphy v. Tenn. Dep't of Revenue


No. M2009-01901-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 443


June 1, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
July 13, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Murphy v. Tenn. Dep't of Revenue, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1181 (Tenn., Dec. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Appeal Dismissed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 08-1019-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former judge filed an action to contest the determination by appellee department that he was not entitled to have a judicial license plate for his vehicle. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) upheld the administrative decision based on former Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-4-226(f) (2004). The former judge appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department asserted that the appeal should have been dismissed because the issue was no longer justiciable as § 55-4-226(f) was amended during the pendency of this dispute and presently in effect allowed former municipal court judges, whether appointed or elected, to have judicial license plates. The appellate court agreed. The 2004 statute was superseded on July 1, 2009, while the case was pending in the trial court. Regrettably, it appeared that the parties and the chancery court were unaware of the 2009 amendment. The 2009 amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-4-226(f) provided the relief that the former judge was seeking; therefore, the issues on appeal were moot.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1097 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Cooper


No. M2009-00915-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 438


January 8, 2010, Session 
July 9, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Doe v. Cooper, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1194 (Tenn., Dec. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 08 C 730. Joe Binkley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of five counts of indecent exposure under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-511 when indecent exposure was not classified as a sexual offense. Three years after his convictions, the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) found that the retroactive application of the Tennessee Sexual Offender Registration, Verification, and Tracking Act of 2004, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-39-201 et seq., was constitutional. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: When petitioner was convicted, the Sexual Offender Registration and Monitoring Act of 1994 was in effect. The 1994 Act did not classify indecent exposure as a sexual offense. Unlike the prior Act, the 2004 Act classified persons convicted of at least three indecent exposure offenses as sexual offenders. It required all persons classified as sexual offenders to register with the sex offender registry, and it prohibited sexual offenders whose victims were minors from working or residing within 1,000 feet of a school, child care facility, or public park. The victim of one of petitioner's convictions was a minor. The 2004 Act was part of a nonpunitive regulatory framework that did not constitute punishment. Therefore, the classification, registration, and employment restraint provisions of the 2004 Act, as retroactively applied to petitioner, were constitutional and did not violate U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, cl. 1 or Tenn. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1098 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Teco Barge Line, Inc. v. Wilson


No. M2009-01675-COA-R12-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 435


April 16, 2010, Session 
July 9, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Teco Barge Line, Inc. v. Morgan, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1185 (Tenn., Dec. 7, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by TECO Barge Line, Inc. v. Wilson, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3175 (U.S., Apr. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 12 Direct Review of Administrative Proceedings by the Court of Appeals; Judgment of the Tennessee State Board of Equalization Assessment Appeals Commission Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Tennessee State Board of Equalization. Assessment Appeals Commission. Kelsie Jones, Executive Secretary.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Tennessee State Board of Equalization Assessment Appeals Commission Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, an interstate water transportation carrier company, was assessed an ad valorem tax on personal property by appellee treasurer. The taxpayer appealed to the Tennessee State Board of Equalization Assessment Appeals Commission. The taxpayer was then retroactively assessed for the two tax years preceding the original assessment. The assessments were upheld and the taxpayer sought the court's review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer asserted on appeal that the tax imposed by Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-1301, as applied to it, violated the federal and state constitutions, and that taxes assessed pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1002 were imposed in retaliation for its appeal. The court upheld the constitutionality of § 67-5-1301 because it was applied to an activity with a substantial nexus with the taxing state, was fairly apportioned, did not discriminate against interstate commerce, and was fairly related to the services provided by the state. The court further held that governmental action could be a tort if motivated in substantial part by a desire to punish an individual for exercising a constitutional right. The retroactive assessments were imposed after the taxpayer had exercised its right under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-1327 to appeal the original assessment, and the taxpayer was the only water carrier of the seven originally assessed that exercised its statutory right to appeal and was the only one assessed back taxes. That evidence was sufficient to infer that the reexamination of the taxpayer's operations prior to the original assessment was prompted by the appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed to the extent that it upeld the ad valorem property tax assessments against the taxpayer for the tax years 2005-2008. The judgment was reversed regarding the Commission's decision to uphold the assessments for the years 2003 and 2004.

Wicker v. Comm'r, Tenn. Dep't of Revenue


No. M2009-02305-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


342 S.W.3d 35; 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 397


May 25, 2010, Session 
June 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Wicker v. Comm'r, Tenn. Dep't of Revenue, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1047 (Tenn., Nov. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Maury County. No. 08-888. Jim T. Hamilton, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed an action under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1801 in the Chancery Court for Maury County (Tennessee) against defendant Tennessee Department of Revenue for a refund of taxes assessed and paid under the Drug Tax, which was declared unconstitutional. The trial court granted the taxpayers' motion for class certification. The Department filed an interlocutory appeal challenging certification.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were assessed and paid a Drug Tax on unauthorized substances and illicit alcoholic beverages pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2801. The tax was later declared unconstitutional. Both taxpayers filed claims for a refund. The Department attempted to issue refund checks. The taxpayers sued on behalf of all who had not been fully refunded and who had not reached a formal, final settlement of their refund. The trial court ordered the Department to turn certain information regarding purported class members over to the taxpayers under seal. On appeal, the Department alleged that the taxpayers' sole remedies were specifically set forth in the Taxpayer Remedies Statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1801 et seq. The taxpayers alleged that, although not specifically set forth in the statute, a class action was an option. The appellate court agreed with the Department that, if the legislature intended to permit a class action, it would have included that option in the statute. Because the trial court's certification of the class disregarded the explicit procedures for challenging tax liabilities established by the legislature, the certification was improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment certifying the action as a class action.

 

1100 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Dana Corp. v. Chumley


No. M2009-00888-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 371


February 23, 2010, Session 
May 28, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-3225-III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought judicial review of appellee Tennessee Commissioner of Revenue's denial of its claim for job tax credits. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted the Commissioner summary judgment. The taxpayer sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer asserted that under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2109(c)(2)(A), it was entitled to job tax credits it created through its acquisition of a corporation. The trial court held that the taxpayer, as a successor to the corporation that originally earned the credits, was barred by § 67-4-2109(e)(1) from using the remaining credits for the years at issue. The appellate court agreed that under § 67-4-2109(e)(1), no job tax credit was available to taxpayers claiming the credit as successor entities. As § 67-4-2109(e)(1) was in effect when the taxpayer's liability was determined, the trial court properly applied it and did not thereby violate Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20's ban on retrospective laws, because § 67-4-2109(e)(1) neither impaired the obligation of contracts nor affected vested rights. Even assuming the taxpayer would have been entitled to its predecessor's unused credits under prior law, that eligibility was eliminated when § 67-4-2109(e)(1) was enacted, and any unused credits were lost. As the Commissioner prevailed on the matters in controversy, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1803(d) she was entitled to attorney's fees and expenses incurred in the trial court and on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a determination of the attorney's fees and expenses the Commissioner was entitled to recover.
