Byars v. Young


No. W2008-02721-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


327 S.W.3d 42; 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 344


April 20, 2010, Session 
May 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Byars v. Young, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1053 (Tenn., Nov. 10, 2010)
Appeal dismissed by, Without prejudice, Remanded by Byars v. Young, 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 700 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 29, 2013)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by In re T.R.Y., 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 76 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 12, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County. No. M2203. Cary Woods, Referee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed from an order of the Juvenile Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) designating defendant father as a minor child's primary residential parent, with no provision for parenting time for the mother.


OVERVIEW: Following entry of the order, the mother appealed to the circuit court. After several years, the case was transferred and the appeal was dismissed. The mother again appealed and the circuit court transferred the matter to the court of appeals. The circuit court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear the appeal, and, thus, its orders were null and void. Accordingly, only the issues with respect to the juvenile court proceedings were considered. The appellate record consisted only of the technical record; there was no transcript or statement of the evidence. Accordingly, a presumption arose that sufficient evidence supported the juvenile court's findings. Because the mother refused to accept that her accusations of sexual abuse against the father were unfounded and because the mother's repeated accusations were destructive to the father's relationship with the child, the juvenile court did not err in designating the father as the primary residential parent. However, the juvenile court erred in not including a grant of residential parenting time to the mother. The juvenile court's factual findings did not justify precluding the mother from having any visitation whatsoever.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the designation of the father as the primary residential parent, but reversed that portion of the order relating to parenting time. It remanded the matter to the juvenile court for entry of an order providing for parenting time for the mother.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the administratrix of a decedent's estate, filed an action against defendant nursing home, asserting claims of negligence and wrongful death. OVERVIEW: The decedent died after being removed from the nursing home. It also moved to stay all proceedings, arguing that all claims were barred by the parties' alternative dispute resolution (ADR) agreement. Rather, the nursing home moved the trial court to limit discovery and to dismiss the complaint as barred by the alleged ADR agreement.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals dismissed the appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Wayman v. Transp. Licensing Comm'n of the Metro. Gov't of Nashville

2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 251

Tenn. R. App. P. Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 09-386-1. Claudia C. Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner operator sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellees, government and county, and upheld the revocation of the operator's license to operate a wrecker service.


OVERVIEW: The Transportation Licensing Commission (Commission) revoked the operator's license to operate a wrecker service, the chancery court upheld the revocation, and the appellate court affirmed. The Commission observed that the signatures on a towing slip and letter that purportedly belonged to an individual clearly did not match. The Commission found the operator guilty of towing a vehicle without proper authorization and suspended his license for 12 months, in part, for two counts of violating Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-16-112. Transportation Licensing Commission of Metropolitan Government of Nashville and Davidson County Rule 24 provided that there could be no relationship between the agent of a property owner designated to authorize towing from private property without consent of the vehicle owner and the towing company. The individual who allegedly signed the slip was the sister of the operator's employee and she apparently resided at the same home as the operator, or at least used his mailing address. A person exercising ordinary common sense would understand that the individual was a person with whom the operator had some relationship.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Proffitt v. Smoky Mt. Woodcarvers Supply, Inc.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 234


September 17, 2009, Session

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Blount County. No. E-22595. W. Dale Young, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholder filed an action against defendant corporation pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-26-104 (2002), requesting the Circuit Court for Blount County (Tennessee) to summarily order that she could inspect and copy corporate records and to award her costs and reasonable attorney fees. The corporation challenged the trial court's order finding that the shareholder complied with § 48-26-104(a) and requiring it to comply with her request.


OVERVIEW: No summons was ever issued to the corporation pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 4. A copy of the complaint was sent to the corporation's attorney for Woodcarvers, but no summons was served. The attorney informed the shareholder's attorney that he could not accept service for the corporation. The corporation appeared specially to file a motion to dismiss asserting lack of jurisdiction over the person, insufficiency of process, and insufficiency of service of process. On appeal, it contended that the trial court did not have in personam jurisdiction over it because no service of process was ever issued nor was the complaint provided to it. The court of appeals agreed, holding that the corporation was never before the trial court as a party. Without jurisdiction, the orders entered in the matter were void. To allow the trial court to issue orders without notice to the corporation rendered useless the defenses in Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12 regarding jurisdiction and process.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals reversed the orders of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Tigrett v. Linn


No. W2009-00205-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 240


January 22, 2010, Session 
March 31, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 - Interlocutory Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Vacated in Part and Remanded. Interlocutory Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-004155-04. Kay S. Robilio, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Vacated in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient filed a medical malpractice action against appellants, an optometrist and an ophthalmologist. Appellants moved for summary judgment, arguing that the complaint was barred by the statute of repose, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-116(a)(3). They challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied the motion, finding that the statute was tolled due to their fraudulent concealment.


OVERVIEW: The patient had LASIK surgery. A few years later, he began to experience eye pain, blurred vision, and uncontrollable eye movement. He was informed that he could be developing Keratoconus. The court of appeals held that the patient submitted sufficient evidence to create an issue of fact as to appellants' knowledge of his condition prior to surgery. Two experts opined that the pre-operative reports clearly showed that the patient had Keratoconus and that any doctor complying with the standard of care should have known of his condition. Even assuming that appellants did not know of the patient's condition prior to surgery, there was at least a question of fact as to their knowledge and possible fraudulent concealment after the surgery. An expert opined that appellants misled the patient in informing him that the surgery was successful and by telling him years after the surgery that it had no harmful effect on his vision. The patient had to prove actual knowledge of the condition in order to proceed under fraudulent concealment, and it was not enough for him to show that appellants should have known. However, that actual knowledge could be inferred from the facts and circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's denial of the motions for summary judgment, but it vacated any decision that the statute of repose was tolled as a result of fraudulent concealment.

Campbell v. Teague


No. W2009-00529-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 239


January 20, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
March 31, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3. Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Henderson County. No. 18534. James F. Butler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, builders, sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Henderson County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellees, homeowners, and awarded them damages under the Tennessee Consumer Protection Act (TCPA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-101 et seq., and arising from the builders' breach of warranty and contract.


OVERVIEW: In a construction action, the builders appealed the trial court's award of damages to the homeowners pursuant to the TCPA, and stemming from the builders' breach of warranty and contract. The appellate court affirmed. Because it could not be found that Henderson County was an exempt county under Tenn. Code. Ann. § 62-6-102(D) (2002), there was sufficient proof, beyond a licensing issue, from which the trial court could have concluded that the builders' practices were in violation of the TCPA. There was also ample evidence to support the finding that the builders acted in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-104(b)(7) by representing that the goods and services were of a particular standard, while they were not, and in violation of § 47-18-104(b)(27) by engaging in deceptive acts and practices. Consequently, the trial court did not err in awarding the homeowners' attorney fees under the TCPA. The preponderance of the evidence supported the trial court's award of $ 52,804.75 in attorney fees and $ 11,297.82 in expenses. It was clear that no waiver of the implied warranty of good workmanship and material was present in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and remanded for a determination of attorney fees. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the builders.

 

1108 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Constr. Crane & Tractor, Inc. v. Wirtgen Am., Inc.


No. M2009-01131-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 213


January 7, 2010, Session 
March 24, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 07-2151-I. Claudia Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant distributor sought review of an order of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissing its action against appellee manufacturer, which sought an injunction and declaratory judgment following the manufacturer's termination of its sales and service agreement with the distributor without cause. The distributor asserted that the termination violated the Tennessee Dealer Protection Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1301 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1302, a 1999 amendment to the Tennessee Dealer Protection Act, manufacturers were prohibited from terminating a dealer's relationship with the manufacturer without cause. The provision was inapplicable to the parties in the instant action because the operative agreement between the parties predated the 1999 amendment. The controlling agreement between the parties was entered into in 1992. Contrary to the distributor's contention, the parties did not mutually assent to a new agreement after 1999, and the 1992 agreement was not modified or amended by mutual assent or course of dealing at any time after 1999. Accordingly, the 1992 agreement was still the operative agreement between the parties. Because Tennessee law permitted the manufacturer to exercise its right under the 1992 agreement to terminate the distributor without cause when the 1992 agreement was entered into, it would have been an unconstitutional impairment of the manufacturer's contractual rights under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20, to apply the current Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1302 to the 1992 agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

OVERVIEW: The father asserted that the trial court erred by failing to apply the superior parental rights doctrine in this case. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed from a judgment of the Chancery Court for Maury County, Tennessee, which modified the parties' parenting plan and reduced the father's child support in accordance with the current child support guidelines.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court erred in finding that a material change in circumstance had occurred, that the court abused its discretion by not permitting the parties' older child to testify, and that the trial court failed to consider the best interests of the children. The instant court found that the record was devoid of any indication that the trial court considered the preferences of the older child, or that the trial court exercised its discretion when it simply stated that it did not want to hear the child's testimony. Further, in light of the offer of proof contained in the record, and in light of the entirety of the circumstances of this case, the instant court agreed that the preferences of the child must be considered by the court in order to determine whether modification of the parenting plan was in the children's best interest, as opposed to their parents'. Next, the instant court found that the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that the wife was voluntarily unemployed where it was undisputed that the wife made no attempt to rehabilitate herself or to seek employment outside the home.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated in part as to the finding that a material change of circumstances had occurred such that modification of the parenting plan to substantially increase the father's parenting time was in the children's best interest, and remanded for further proceedings regarding the bests interests of the children.

Redmon v. City of Memphis


No. W2009-01520-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 122


January 21, 2010, Session 
February 19, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-08-2201-2. Arnold Goldin, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city employee (employee) sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee city and upheld the employee's termination.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated after accessing a city-owned database to obtain the telephone number of a police officer who had arrested her husband and calling the officer at his home to inquire about the arrest. Her termination was upheld and the appellate court further affirmed. She claimed that the Civil Service Commission (Commission) violated State law when it deliberated over her appeal in private. However, the Commission should not be viewed as a governing body subject to the Open Meetings Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101 et seq. The employee's claim that the trial court failed to indicate any substantial and material evidence upon which the commission relied to reach its decision was rejected. Access to city-owned computer equipment was to be used exclusively for business purposes and the employee had no legitimate business reason for accessing the officer's confidential information to inquire about her husband's arrest and doing so violated city policy. Further, because the opportunity to call witnesses was discretionary, her due process rights were not violated by her supervisor's decision to disallow witnesses at the fact-finding hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and costs of the appeal were taxed to the employee.

State ex rel. Bd. of Educ. v. City of Memphis


No. W2009-00366-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


329 S.W.3d 465; 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 13


October 14, 2009, Session 
January 13, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State ex rel. Bd. of Educ. v. City of Memphis, 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 820 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 10, 2010)
Appeal denied by State ex rel. Bd. of Educ. of the Memphis City Schs v. City of Memphis, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 788 (Tenn., Aug. 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-08-1139-3. Kenny W. Armstrong, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the City of Memphis, Tennessee (city) and the Memphis City Council (city council), sought judicial review of a writ of mandamus from the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) ordering the city to restore funding to the Memphis City Schools (schools) for the 2008-09 school year in compliance with Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 49-2-203 and 49-3-314. The writ was granted pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 54.02.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the statutorily mandated school funding provisions contained in §§ 49-3-314(c) and 49-2-203(a)(10)(A)(ii), the anti-supplanting statutes, and the maintenance of effort (MOE) provisions, were applicable to the city, as a local government. The city charter authorized the city to provide funding to the schools through an ad valorem tax. The city argued unsuccessfully that it was not required to provide funding to the schools under either its charter or the general education statutes. Section 773 of the city charter clearly reflected the General Assembly's intention that the city assume some obligation for funding of the schools though an ad valorem tax. The city also argued unsuccessfully that it was not a local government for the purposes of the general education statutes, and that the statutory scheme applied only to the county governments. The city was governed by the anti-supplanting provisions found in the Tennessee Code and the MOE rule. Both the county and the city were required to fund the schools in conformance with the Basic Education Program, the anti-supplanting statutes, and the MOE provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, and costs of the appeal were taxed against the city and the city council.

Waters v. Ray


No. M2008-02086-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 888


November 16, 2009, Submitted on Briefs 
December 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Waters v. Ray, 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 85 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 25, 2010)
Appeal denied by Waters v. Ray, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 859 (Tenn., Sept. 2, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-2083-III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.
Waters v. Ray, 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 366 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 25, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from an order of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granting summary judgment in favor of respondents, a warden and the Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Corrections (TDOC), and denying the inmate's motion to alter or amend in the inmate's declaratory judgment action, arguing that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-25-143 (2006) was unconstitutionally applied retroactively to him.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was found guilty of various crimes and the court costs from his criminal trial were billed in part to the State. Three years later, the State informed the inmate that, in accordance with § 40-25-143, TDOC would begin deducting amounts from his inmate trust fund account to reimburse the State. Section 40-25-143 became effective one month after the inmate's criminal trial. He asserted that under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-25-129(1), he acquired a vested interest in having the State pay the court costs billed in his criminal trial and, therefore, TDOC was estopped to collect funds from his trust account. However, the statutory exceptions in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-25-129 were permissive, and not mandatory derogations from the general rule. Section 40-25-129 states that a criminal court may bill costs to the State when a felony prosecution has proceeded to a verdict; it does not require the criminal court to do so. Even if costs were billed to the State, subsequent recovery from the convicted defendant was not precluded pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-25-123(a) (2006). Accordingly, the trial court did not err in dismissing the petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Crosby v. Holt

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamblen County. No. 2007-350. John S. McLellan, III, Judge.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public school teacher (teacher) sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Hamblen County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellees, the board of education and its members (board), and upheld the teacher's discharge.


OVERVIEW: The teacher appealed his termination by the board pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-5-513 (2009) but the chancery court upheld the discharge as warranted on the grounds of unprofessional conduct and insubordination under Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-5-511(a)(1), (2) (2009). The teacher's actions involved, allegedly, an inappropriate relationship with a minor female student, improper e-mails sent over the school's system, and inaccurate information that the teacher supplied during the investigation of the allegations. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the notice of charges in the memorandum from a department of education director to the board, as supplemented by the interviews of the teacher, were sufficient to allow him to prepare his defense. There was compelling proof, albeit largely circumstantial, of a sexual relationship between the student and the teacher. Further, the teacher offered no authority for the proposition that a school may not interfere with nonsexual association between a student and a teacher based on concerns of parents, even if the concerns were exaggerated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and costs on appeal are taxed to the teacher. The case was remanded for collection of costs assessed below.

City of Harriman v. Roane County Election Comm'n


No. E2008-02316-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 877


November 4, 2009, Session 
December 28, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by City of Harriman v. Roane County Election Comm'n, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 709 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2010)
Reversed by City of Harriman v. Roane County Election Comm'n, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 576 (Tenn., June 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Roane County. No. 16010. Frank V. Williams, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought review of a judgment from the chancery court for Roane County (Tennessee), which found in favor of defendant town and dismissed plaintiff's action seeking to void defendant's referendum without reaching the issue of priority. The action involved a contest between plaintiff and defendant, which were neighboring towns, over a common territory that both purported to have annexed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant sought to add the territory through a referendum election, plaintiff used its annexation ordinance. Plaintiff asserted that its ordinance took priority because it , was granted statutory priority. Defendant argued that plaintiff's ordinance was of no effect. Upon review, the court held that, Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-58-111(c) (Supp. 2009), provided an exception to the general rule against expanding outside a growth plan that allowed a municipality to annex outside its urban growth boundary. A municipality qualified for that exception by following the procedure in § 6-58-111(d). To follow the procedure of § 6-58-111(d) the municipality had to first propose an amendment to its urban growth boundary or conduct its annexation by referendum. Finally, a municipality qualified under § 6-58-111(d)(1) if it has acted under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-58-104(d)(1) to propose an amendment to the growth plan by filing an appropriate notice. Thus, trial court erred in finding that a municipality had to amend its urban growth boundary following the procedures in § 6-58-104 and plaintiff qualified under § 6-58-111(d)(1) to annex by ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1116 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Grusin


No. W2009-00033-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 874


October 28, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
December 22, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-004288-06. Karen R. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff successor trustee filed an action against defendants, a broker and a corporation, alleging misappropriation and conversion, breach of fiduciary duty, and civil conspiracy. He challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6).


OVERVIEW: A grantor created a trust. A separate entity was created from the trust. The trust held a fifty percent ownership interest in the separate entity. The grantor consented to the use of the trust's stock for the benefit of the separate entity. The separate entity had an unsecured margin of indebtedness. The trust's stocks were pledged to a bank in return for a loan to the trust. The trust then transferred the loan monies to the separate entity to pay off its indebtedness. The successor trustee argued that his civil conspiracy claim against defendants was improperly dismissed because the trust agreement's exculpatory clause would not affect defendants. The court of appeals held that the successor trustee mistakenly argued that the trial court's dismissal was founded on the exculpatory clause. The trial court's dismissal of the successor trustee's claims was based on its finding that none of the parties engaged in unlawful conduct. Because the successor trustee did not challenge the trial court's finding that defendants' actions were lawful, it would not address the issue. Without an unlawful act by defendants, the successor trustee's civil conspiracy claim failed.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's dismissal.

Johnston v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County


No. M2008-01570-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


320 S.W.3d 299; 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 832


June 23, 2009, Session 
December 10, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Johnston v. Metro. Gov't, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 606 (Tenn., June 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-987-IV. Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner neighborhood residents sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which found in favor of respondents, a local government and the Attorney General for the State of Tennessee (government), in the residents' action challenging the validity of a zoning change based on alleged violations of Tennessee's Open Meeting Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101, et seq.


OVERVIEW: The local government began considering legislation to implement a conservation zoning overlay in a neighborhood. The ordinance adopting the zoning change passed on the first and second reading. Prior to the final meeting on the subject, members of the local government sent numerous emails to each other discussing the proposed zoning change. In addition, some members viewed information on the zoning issue in a non-public conference room. Thereafter the zoning change was adopted at a public meeting. Upon review, the court found that the gathering that took place in the back conference room did not violate the Act; however, some of the email correspondence among members of the local government did violate the Act. Nonetheless, after the exchange of emails, the local government members engaged in a new and substantial reconsideration of the issues surrounding the zoning change; thus the ordinance was not deemed void under the Act. Finally, the court found no violation of the separation of powers doctrine or the due process clause under the Tennessee Constitution, and no abuse of discretion in the trial court's decisions on discovery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the judgment regarding the emails and affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

Green v. Green

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 751

November 4, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Green v. Champs-Elysees, Inc., 2013 Tenn. App. LEXIS 244 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-2817-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.
Green v. Green, 293 S.W.3d 493, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 518 (Tenn., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judgment debtor filed a motion in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) seeking to quash an execution sale and seeking a hearing on his claim of exemptions. Following the execution sale of his stock to defendant judgment creditor, the debtor sought to have the sale set aside. The trial court denied relief, and the debtor appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the case was pending on appeal, the Tennessee Supreme Court reversed the summary judgment against the debtor in the underlying case, which had led to the judgment that the execution sale was held to enforce. The underlying case, which had been brought by the judgment debtor to enforce a purchase of stock, was remanded for a trial on the merits, with some of the questions to be resolved involving the value of the stock, the ownership of the stock, and even the existence and legitimacy of the stock. The creditor contended that the stock issued by the corporation failed to meet statutory requirements. The question of whether any stock was properly issued led to the question of what was exempt from execution and what was sold. Any effort to resolve the issues in the appeal was dependent upon, and subject to revision by, the determination of facts which were before the trial court in the underlying case. The court held that under Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-6-112, the interest which the creditor acquired in the debtor's stock was not affected by the Supreme Court's decision. Thus, on remand, the debtor was entitled to seek recovery of the proceeds of sale, but not the shares of stock.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the trial court and remanded the case for consideration in light of the issues to be determined in the underlying case.

Wright v. City of Shelbyville


No. M2009-00321-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 744


August 5, 2009, Session 
November 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Wright v. City of Shelbyville, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 398 (Tenn., Apr. 14, 2010)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Wright v. City of Shelbyville Bd. of Zoning Appeals, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 763 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Bedford County. No. 25,630. Lee Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, appealed from the Chancery Court for Bedford County, TN, and challenged an amendment to a zoning ordinance affecting their property on the ground that the content of the published notice was inadequate in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-203. Appellees, the city, a city council, and a planning commission, opposed.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented required a two-step analysis. First, the court had to determine what type of notice was required in order to amend zoning restrictions under the governing statutes. The second step was then to decide whether the notice published in the local newspaper met this standard. The appellate court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-203(a) required that the published notice of a change in permitted land use must be specific or complete enough to enable the average person to determine whether his or her property might be affected by the proposed change. The point of departure for determining whether the published notice for the ordinance was adequate was the language of the publication itself. Based on the published notice for the ordinance at issue, that landowners in the I-2 zoning district, including the property owners, were not apprised that the proposed amendment might affect their property. Failure to substantially comply with statutory requirements rendered the zoning ordinance invalid.


OUTCOME: The trial court was reversed and the ordinance was declared invalid. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the city, the city council, and the planning commission.

Siegel-Robert, Inc. v. Johnson


No. M2008-02228-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 722


August 5, 2009, Session 
October 28, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-2356-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
Swope v. Siegel-Robert, Inc., 74 F. Supp. 2d 876, 1999 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15973 (E.D. Mo., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought a complaint against defendant state in which it sought a tax refund for an overpayment of taxes assessed on "nonbusiness earnings." The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tenn.) granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a corporation that operated through several divisions, including one engaged in the manufacture of decorative plastic parts for automobiles. The taxpayer's corporate headquarters and commercial domicile was St. Louis, Missouri. As part of its business operations, the taxpayer utilized a practice whereby funds not needed for operational purposes were invested in Treasury securities. The state asserted that the interest income from short-term investments in Treasury securities constituted business earnings. The appellate court found that the materials submitted by the taxpayer in support of its motion for summary judgment showed that the income earned from the investment in Treasury securities was not used to fund the operations of the automotive division or to acquire businesses related to, or for the purpose of expanding, the automotive division. The state's speculative contention that the taxpayer used the income earned from the investment in Treasury securities in the operation of the automotive division was not sufficient to create an actual relation between the use of the income and the operations conducted in Tennessee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Shelton v. Rutherford County


No. M2008-02596-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 706


July 7, 2009, Session 
October 23, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County. No. 08-0884 CV. Robert E. Corlew, III, Chancellor.
Shelton v. Rutherford County, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 81519 (M.D. Tenn., Sept. 8, 2009)
Shelton v. Rutherford County, 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 811 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 18, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee), which vacated a county board of commissioners' decision denying appellee property owner's application for rezoning, which award the owners attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. §§1983 and 1988, and which remanded the matter for further consideration.


OVERVIEW: The owners filed an application for rezoning to allow the development of an amusement park. The owners challenged the denial of their application and the validity of Rutherford County, Tenn., Zoning Resolution § 4.05 pursuant to which the county commission required a two-thirds vote for passage of the application. The court found that the rezoning application would substantially affect the use of the land, and thus, even if Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-105 did not apply, the same result would be reached under Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-5-109(a), a provision requiring a majority vote for all business before the county legislative body. Neither the county's grant of authority to enact zoning ordinances nor its general legislative authority allowed it to impose a supermajority requirement with respect to zoning amendments. The court held that § 4.05 was not within the Tennessee General Assembly's grant of authority to the county and was therefore ultra vires and avoid ab initio. The owner's zoning application received a majority vote of the commission and should have been declared to have passed. There should not have been an award of attorney fees as there were no constitutional violations.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trail court's decision and remanded with instructions that the trial court direct the county commissioners to declare the zoning application granted.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff entertainment businesses sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granting defendant local governments' motion to dismiss under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6) for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The businesses had filed an action against the governments challenging Metro. Gov't Nashville & Davidson County, Tenn., Code Laws ch. 6.54.


OVERVIEW: Chapter 6.54 governed the licensing and regulation of sexually oriented businesses. The businesses alleged that ch. 6.54 was unconstitutional, both facially and as applied, under the Tennessee Constitution for violations of their rights to free speech, expression, privacy, association, equal protection, and due process. Upon review, the court determined that the businesses failed to state any as applied constitutional claims upon which relief cold be granted because the businesses asserted no facts to support their claims. The court noted that ch. 6.54 contained 35 definitions and that the businesses failed to identify which of the 35 definitions they contended to be facially invalid under the Tennessee Constitution. The court concluded that the pleading requirements set forth in Tenn. R. Civ. P. 8.05 were not satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Tennessee Department of Revenue (Department) sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which awarded appellee taxpayer a refund, as well as statutory interest, of a tax imposed under the Excise Tax Law, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2001, et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Department assessed an excise tax on the taxpayer, a nondomiciliary subsidiary corporation conducting business in the State of Tennessee, based on income earned outside the State as a result of the parent corporation's redemption of outstanding stock held by the taxpayer. The Department's tax assessment was based on a determination that the income was taxable as business earnings. The court held that while there was evidence of overlap in the management of the entities, the record did not reflect sufficient control on the part of the parent over the taxpayer's activities in Tennessee to support a finding of centralized management for purposes of the hallmarks of a unitary relationship test. In addition, the record did not contain sufficient evidence to prove that the taxpayer realized any benefits as a result of a reorganization or a stock redemption which contributed to the taxpayer's operations or which taxpayer depended on in performing its operation, so as to justify a finding that the parent and the taxpayer were functionally integrated. There was not evidence that the parent provided any central serviced to the taxpayer which undermined its operation independence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Person v. Bd. of Comm'rs


No. W2007-01346-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 652


June 24, 2008, Session 
September 28, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Person v. Bd. of Comm'rs of Shelby County, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 290 (Tenn., Mar. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-06-2237-3. Kenny W. Armstrong, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile court judge filed suit against appellees, the mayor and the county board of commissioners, challenging a resolution passed by the board that resulted in a second juvenile court division (division 2). The Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) found that § 20 of Chapter 219 of the Private Acts of 1967 (Private Act) was constitutional and lifted a temporary injunction. The judge appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge argued that the trial court erred when it found § 20 of the Private Act to be constitutional and the judge appealed the trial court's order which quashed his discovery request upon the determination that the Open Meetings Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101 et seq., claim was mooted by the board's decision to rescind the resolution. As a judge was a necessary component of a court, in order to ordain and establish a court under Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 1, the legislation creating or establishing the court must make provision for a judge. The legislature could not establish a court without also establishing a judgeship. Since § 20 of the Private Act did not create or establish a judgeship for division 2, it did not effectively create or establish that division or court. Also because in § 20 the legislature delegated to the board the power to decide whether a judge for division 2 was needed, which was the equivalent of delegating to the board the authority to establish or create division 2, § 20 was an unconstitutional delegation of power reserved to the General Assembly by art. VI, § 1. The trial court's dismissal of the Open Meetings Act claim as moot was affirmed.


OUTCOME: On the constitutional issue, the trial court was reversed, and § 20 of the Private Act was found to be unconstitutional. Consequently, the resolution enacted pursuant to § 20 was invalid and of no effect. The trial court's dismissal of the Open Meetings Act claim was affirmed. Costs of appeal were assessed against appellees for which execution might issue if necessary.

Robbins v. Farr


No. M2006-01730-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 536


May 31, 2007, Session 
August 11, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-2363-IV. Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, an alleged drug dealer, sought a declaratory judgment with respect to a tax assessment. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, agreed with the alleged drug dealer. Appellant Commission of Revenue appealed.


OVERVIEW: The alleged drug dealer was arrested by federal authorities pursuant to an indictment charging him and a co-defendant with possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. The Commissioner assessed a tax against the alleged drug dealer pursuant to Tennessee's tax on being found in possession of untaxed, unauthorized substances, codified at Tennessee Code Annotated § 67-4-2801, et seq. The alleged drug dealer brought a constitutional challenge to Tennessee's "Drug Tax." The supreme court held the tax to be unconstitutional because it could not be classified as either a tax on merchants and peddlers, or a tax on a privilege, as authorized by the Tennessee Constitution. Specifically, the supreme court found that the Drug Tax imposed on "dealers" could not be deemed to be a tax on merchants and peddlers, because the term "dealers" was defined in terms of "possession" of illegal substances, not possession with intent to sell. In other words, the tax is imposed upon the possession, not the merchandising of unauthorized substances, and therefore was not a tax on merchants and peddlers.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

Marra v. Bank of N.Y.


No. W2008-00773-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


310 S.W.3d 329; 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 529


January 22, 2009, Session 
August 4, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Marra v. Bank of N.Y., 310 S.W.3d 329, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 909 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2009)
Appeal denied by Marra v. Bank of N.Y., 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 214 (Tenn., Feb. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Fayette County. No. 14216. William C. Cole, Chancellor.
Marra v. Bank of New York, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 827 (Tenn. Ct. App., Sept. 18, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee homeowner sued appellants, bank and trustee, after they held a foreclosure sale without proper notice to the homeowner. The bank appealed the Chancery Court for Fayette County, Tennessee's order that the clerk be awarded a fee for facilitating the sale and named the clerk as an appellee. The clerk's motion for Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11 sanctions was granted. The bank's cross-motions for sanctions were denied. The bank and the trustee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it awarded the clerk a $ 14,450 fee for his services pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-21-401(i)(7) (2002) because the statute gave the trial court the authority to award a fee to the clerk for his services, with the amount to be within the trial court's discretion, so long as the fee is within the statutory parameters. The trial court chose to award the clerk 5 percent of the purchase price of the sale, well within the 10 percent authorized under the statute. The trial court abused its discretion when it granted the clerk's Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11 motion for sanctions and awarded appellate attorney's fees to the clerk for the trustee's filing of pleadings in connection with the first appeal because the clerk's motion for sanctions was in essence a motion for appellate attorney's fees pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-1-122 for the filing of a frivolous appeal and under § 27-1-122, the decision on whether to award damages for the filing of a frivolous appeal rested solely in the discretion of the appellate court, and it was improper for the trial court to essentially grant appellate attorney's fees to the clerk under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed as to the trial court's award of appellate attorney's fees as sanctions. All other decisions by the trial court were affirmed. Costs on appeal were taxed one half to the bank and its surety, and one half to the homeowner.

Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth.


No. E2008-00525-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 521


November 6, 2008, Session 
July 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth., 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 980 (Tenn., Oct. 12, 2010)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth., 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 604 (Tenn., Jan. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 05C556. W. Jeffrey Hollingsworth, Judge.
Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 114 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees, two former criminal investigators for a housing authority, sued defendants, the authority and a supervisor for wrongful termination and other claims. The Circuit Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, granted summary judgment for defendants, and plaintiffs appealed. The court withdrew a prior opinion and replaced it with the current opinion.


OVERVIEW: The court held that summary judgment was properly granted on one employee's defamation claim against the supervisor because the supervisor had statutory immunity under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-1003 to the extent that the claim arose from a letter to the Tennessee Peace Officer Standards and Training (POST) Commission. The termination was also not actionable in a claim against the supervisor for interfering with the employment relationship because the employee's violation of the employer's cell phone policy was more than enough to justify termination, even if the supervisor was involved and had some element of ill will. There was a dispute of fact as to whether it was profiling when the authority told the employees to issue a criminal trespass citation or arrest and jail every male between the ages of 18 and 35 that came into a housing development. However, the employees' whistleblower claim failed because there was unrebutted evidence of non-pretextual reasons for the terminations and only circumstantial evidence of a causal connection. The causal connection was sufficiently supported, however, for a claim under the Tennessee Human Rights Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-301.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the supervisor on the claim of defamation; affirmed the grant of summary judgment as to the claims against the supervisor for inducement of breach of contract; affirmed summary judgment to the authority as to the whistleblower claims; and vacated summary judgment to the authority as to the claims under the THRA. This case was remanded for further proceedings.

Millennium Taxi Serv., L.L.C. v. Chattanooga Metro. Airport Auth.


No. E2008-00838-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 413


February 10, 2009, Session 
June 30, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 05C1445. W. Neil Thomas, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, granted in part and denied in part summary judgment to appellee Chattanooga Metropolitan Airport Authority (CMAA) upon finding that the challenged regulations by appellant taxi service had a rational basis and did not discriminate unreasonably against unregistered taxis. The service appealed.


OVERVIEW: The service argued that the CMAA Regulations violated equal protection principles by prohibiting only non-registered taxis from conducting curbside passenger pickups, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1; Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 and art. XI, § 8. The appellate court found that the Regulations authorized registered taxis to park, wait, and pick up their next fare in a designated taxi zone at the curbside outside the baggage claim area. Taxis not registered were not subject to such regulations and requirements and were effectively removed from access to incoming passengers unless the passengers had made advance reservations. The Regulations were reasonably related to their legitimate purpose of presenting incoming passengers with transportation options, whether they be taxis, limousines, or other vehicles, from providers that were known to CMAA to have vehicles that were relatively new, clean, and in good repair -- conditions imposed upon all permitted commercial ground transportation vehicles. CMAA had taken steps to ensure that incoming passengers who had not made advance arrangements would be presented as a first option with registered and therefore, regulated, transportation providers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Smith v. Pratt


No. M2008-01540-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 144


February 17, 2009, Session 
April 22, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 04C-2961. Barbara Haynes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient sued her surgeon's estate for malpractice and appellant hospital for allowing the surgeon to practice in its facilities. The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied the hospital's motion for summary judgment and ruled that the hospital was not eligible for the qualified immunity provided in Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-6-219(d)(1). The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient received plastic surgery to remove excess skin on her body due to weight loss. After she was discharged, she developed serious complications. She filed a malpractice action against her doctor's estate. She also sued the hospital, alleging that it should not have granted surgical privileges to the doctor because he was incompetent and dangerous. The hospital filed a motion for summary judgment claiming Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-6-219 provided qualified immunity for credentialing decisions. The trial court erred by denying the motion. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee held that the plain language of Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-6-219(d)(1) supported the interpretation that the qualified immunity applied when a patient sued a hospital for a peer review committee's credentialing decision. The qualified immunity defense under Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-6-219(d)(1) was constitutional under the open courts clause of the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1131 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Seramur v. Life Care Ctrs. of Am., Inc.


No. E2008-01364-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 126


February 11, 2009, Session 
April 2, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Bradley County. No. 06-199. Hon. Jerri S. Bryant, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Bradley County, Tennessee, granted defendant employer summary judgment on plaintiff employee's action to enforce an employment contract for benefits allegedly due under the contract on the grounds that a provision in the employment contract was an unenforceable contract, as the provision amounted to an agreement to agree and dismissed the action. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee asked the appellate court to reverse the granting of summary judgment because the contract provided that the employer would give a 25% ownership interest in a nursing home to the employee, and he argued that the terms of the contract between the parties as to the ownership interest were reasonably certain and provided a basis for determining the existence of a breach and for providing an appropriate remedy. The appellate court found that the undisputed facts demonstrated that the agreement entered into between the employee and employer to choose a facility by mutual consent was so indefinite and vague as to be unenforceable. The agreement was an agreement to negotiate in the future as to the selection of actual facility and was unenforceable. The employee's reference in the brief to the "annual" distribution or payment of a minimum of $50,000 was not supported by the undisputed provisions of the contract as the language was just too vague to ascertain its meaning. A cause of action under the doctrine of promissory estoppel could not be sustained. The application of the doctrine of elision was inappropriate but harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth.


No. E2008-00525-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 114


November 6, 2008, Session 
March 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Modified by Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 204 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 21, 2009)
Substituted opinion at Sykes v. Chattanooga Hous. Auth., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 521 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 31, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated in Part and Affirmed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 05C556. W. Jeffrey Hollingsworth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated in Part and Affirmed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees, two public safety officers, sued defendant employers, a housing authority and the chief of its safety department, asserting retaliatory discharge claims under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-1-304 (2008) and Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-301(2005), as well as defamation and interference with their contracts of employment. The Circuit Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, granted summary judgment for the employers, and the employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that there was no evidence, for purposes of the claim under the Whistleblower Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-1-304 (2008), that either employee was asked or required to participate in or remain silent about any illegal activity. The reviewing court held that the statute did not require such evidence. Rather, it was sufficient if the employees had reasonable cause to believe that illegal conduct had occurred or would occur and reported it in good faith. At a minimum, there was a factual dispute as to whether the employees had a reasonable basis to believe that the employer's policy, as applied, was racial profiling. Summary judgment was nevertheless appropriate as to one employee because the facts showed that he was suspended over the employer's cell phone policy and therefore that retaliation was not the sole cause. As to the retaliation claim under § 4-21-301, the authority failed to negate that the terminations were in retaliation for having opposed discriminatory practices, including illegal arrests based on racial profiling, warrantless searches, and illegal seizures of the mostly African-American residents.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's grant of summary judgment as to one officer's whistleblower claim but affirmed summary judgment as to the other officer's claim under that statute; vacated the grant of summary judgment as to both officers' claims under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-301; vacated the grant of summary judgment as to the claim for inducement of breach of contract; and affirmed summary judgment on the claim of defamation.

Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County v. Allen Family Trust

Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 05C-843. Barbara Haynes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted judgment in favor of appellee Metropolitan Government of Nashville and Davidson County (Metro) by granting Metro's request for an order of possession of appellant property owners' property. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Metro instituted condemnation proceedings against the owners to acquire an easement for the construction of a sewer line. The owners argued that the trial court erred in determining that eminent domain was being exercised for a public use. The owners argued that their failure to question the right to take within five days of service of the petition was the result of excusable neglect and that the trial court abused its discretion in failing to grant them an extension of time within which to question the right to take. The proposed sewer line would become Metro's property, thereby expanding its sewer infrastructure and providing sewer service to a group of Metro residents. Metro's decision to take the easement across the owners' property was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. Nos. 983317, 983400, 033890, 98-3317-III, 03-3890-I-(III), 98-3400-II(III). Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.

OVERVIEW: Metro argued that a United States Supreme Court case abrogated the appellate court's previous ruling and should have been applied on remand. Wade v. Patterson


No. E2007-02893-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 34


September 17, 2008, Session 
January 29, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 06-0707. W. Frank Brown, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, homeowners, sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, a county building commissioner (commissioner), in an action involving the homeowners' rental of their home to vacationers.


OVERVIEW: After the homeowner moved from their residence, they began renting it to vacationers. The commissioner instructed them to cease and desist renting their house for commercial purposes and after the homeowners refused, litigation ensued. The trial court granted the commissioner's motion for summary judgment, finding that the homeowners' use of their house for commercial purposes violated the applicable zoning regulations. The appellate court reversed, finding that the zoning regulations were unconstitutionally vague as applied to the homeowners. The trial court's judgment was, therefore, reversed and the case was dismissed. The appellate court excluded the option that tourist homes were completely prohibited. Since the county intended to allow tourist homes, the regulations were required to provide as least one zone where they were allowed because a complete failure to mention tourist homes resulted in a total prohibition. Unfortunately, the regulations simply did not specify where a tourist home could be located. Thus, the homeowners were left with no alternative but to try and "guess" what the drafters of the regulations intended to do.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and dismissed the case. The case was remanded to the trial court solely for collection of costs below; costs on appeal, as well as those at the trial level, were taxed to the commissioner.

W&T, Inc. v. Ham


No. M2006-01617-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 63


July 8, 2008, Session 
January 29, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Montgomery County. No. MC-CH-CV-FD-06-10. Laurence M. McMillan, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Montgomery County, Tennessee, granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, limited partners, for their action under the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 26-6-101 et seq., to enforce a foreign judgment and to recover attorneys' fees incurred in the enforcement action. Appellant general partners' Tenn. R. Civ. P. 60 motion was denied. The general partners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the judgment rendered in Massachusetts was enforceable in Tennessee. The appellate court noted that under the Act, the judgment of a sister state was entitled to full faith and credit. The parties also agreed that if Massachusetts lacked personal jurisdiction over the general partners, then the Massachusetts judgment was not entitled to full faith and credit and could not be enforced in Tennessee. The appellate court found that Massachusetts had personal jurisdiction over the general partners, who were part of an ongoing continuous business entity with Massachusetts participants that lasted for years. Reports were made on an ongoing basis with the Massachusetts limited partners together with other communications. The parties owned property together. The lawsuit was specifically related to those contacts with the Massachusetts entities that occurred in Massachusetts. The trial court did not err in denying the general partners' objections to domestication of the Massachusetts judgment. The general partners chose not to defend the Massachusetts lawsuit and could not now do so. They did not allege the type of fraud intended by Rule 60.02(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Moses v. City of Jellico


No. E2008-00004-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 19


September 17, 2008, Session 
January 26, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Campbell County. No. 13937. John D. McAfee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city court judge sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Campbell County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee city in the judge's action requesting the trial court to determine if the city had the authority to curtail the city court's jurisdiction and his salary.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance creating the city court pursuant to its power under Private Chapter No. 167 (House Bill No. 3289) of the Private Acts of 2002. When it sought to limit the judge's jurisdiction and salary, the judge sought to prevent the city from doing such. On appeal, the court determined that Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 1 established that the Tennessee General Assembly was authorized to vest judicial power in the courts by ordaining and establishing them. This power involved fundamental principles of our system of governance, including the separation of powers doctrine. The Tennessee General Assembly's constitutional authority to vest judicial power in a lower court could not be delegated to a municipality, but had to be exercised directly by its legislation. Since the city obtained only the power the Tennessee Legislature could delegate, it could exercise no power that the Tennessee Legislature was unable to confer. Accordingly, the city court was not validly created.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Doe v. State


No. E2008-00511-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 1


November 5, 2008, Session, Assigned on Briefs 
January 2, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 168776-1. Hon. John F. Weaver, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The claimant filed an action pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §4-5-322(b)(1)(B)(I), to review actions taken by defendant Tennessee Department of Children's Services (Department). The Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, dismissed the action pursuant to the Department's motion to dismiss. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant alleged that the Department had placed him on a secret, government maintained indicated perpetrator list without affording him due process of law. The trial court found that the claimant's action was not ripe for determination and dismissed the action. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's ruling. There was nothing in the record to indicate that the claimant requested a hearing before being placed on the indicated perpetrator list. In fact, the claimant's original petition stated that after the file review took place and he received notice that his inclusion on the indicated perpetrator list was being upheld, he filed his petition as an appeal directly from this finding. The claimant failed to avail himself of the very administrative remedy which he claimed he was denied, a hearing. Since the claimant failed to timely request a hearing pursuant to Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0250-7-9-.01 et seq., he was deemed to have forever waived his right to a hearing. Also, when and if the Department elected to release the claimant's name as being on the indicated perpetrator list, he would be entitled to notice and would be due a hearing before that action was taken.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Madison A.


No. E2008-01261-COA-R3-PT

Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Washington County. No. J11606. James A. Nidiffer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the Juvenile Court for Washington County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee, the Department of Children's Services, and terminated the mother's parental rights to her daughter.


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the parental rights of the mother to her daughter. The trial court found that the grounds had been proven to terminate the mother's parental rights pursuant to T.C.A. § 36-1-113(g)(8). More specifically, the trial court found that the mother was mentally incompetent to care for the child, and that her mental impairment was likely to remain making it unlikely that she would be able to care for the child in the near future. The trial court also found clear and convincing evidence that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interest. The appellate court affirmed. There were several procedural protections in place to assure that a mentally incompetent parent was afforded due process and the mother was afforded all of those protections. The child's guardian ad litem was required to prove grounds for termination under the clear and convincing evidentiary standard and the mother was appointed both an attorney and a guardian ad litem to protect her interests. Additionally, even with treatment, the mother's mental condition had improved very little and it was not safe for the child to be returned to her care.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Express Disposal, LLC v. City of Memphis


No. W2007-02081-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 772


September 16, 2008, Session 
December 29, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-000558-07. Donna M. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, dismissed appellant garbage collection business' claim for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted against appellee city. The business appealed.


OVERVIEW: The business argued that it had a legal, vested right to conduct its business in the area prior to annexation by the city. It argued that the city had to provide compensation for "taking" its customers and contracts, and for preventing the business from providing its services to residential customers. The appellate court noted that because the business sought compensation for a governmental "taking" although the city had instituted no eminent domain proceedings, the action was classified as one for inverse condemnation. The appellate court found that prior case law did not allow just compensation for any taken intangible "property" rights. Tennessee Code Annotated section 6-51-112(a) required that compensation be paid to electric cooperatives whose property and service rights were "taken" through annexation; however, Tennessee's statutes afford no similar protection to displaced garbage collectors. The appellate court found no support for the business' contention that the city's appropriation of garbage collection services for the area residences constituted a taking, such that just compensation was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
