In re T.M.G.


No. E2008-00865-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


283 S.W.3d 318; 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 713


November 6, 2008, Session 
November 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re T.M.G., 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 86 (Tenn., Feb. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Bradley County. No. 06-177. Jerri S. Bryant, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee great-grandmother of the child obtained temporary custody of the child in 2001. In 2006, the great-grandmother filed suit seeking to terminate the parental rights of appellant father. The Chancery Court for Bradley County (Tennessee) found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(6) was constitutional and terminated the father's parental rights. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father's parental rights were properly terminated under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(6) because he committed a crime and was confined to a correctional facility for 10 or more years and the child was under eight years old when the sentence was imposed. In addition, it was unknown when the father would be released from prison and then how long after his release before he would be able to care for the child, assuming he ever got to that point. Also, although the father maintained some contact with the child, 10 visits over the course of several years could not be described as regular. Furthermore, the child was doing exceedingly well in the care of her great-grandmother and a change of caretakers could indeed have a negative impact on the child's life. Additionally, the great-grandmother's home was a healthy and safe home for the child, and she had a very active role in the child's life. Thus, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(i) (Supp. 2008), the chancery court did not err when it found that the great-grandmother proved by clear and convincing evidence that termination of the father's parental rights was in the child's best interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the chancery court's judgment.

 

1144 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


High Country Adventures, Inc. v. Polk County


No. E2007-02678-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 651


July 22, 2008, Session 
November 10, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by High Country Adventures, Inc. v. Polk County, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 352 (Tenn., May 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Cause Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Polk County. No. 6924. Jerri Bryant, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Polk County, Tennessee, granted appellee Polk County's motion to alter or amend and motion to dismiss on appellant whitewater rafting operator's suit seeking a refund of privilege taxes paid under protest for the 2001 Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-707 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-901. The operators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the question was the trial court erred in granting the county's motion to alter or amend and therefore, its motion to dismiss, upon grounds that the operator was without standing to assert the claims set forth in its complaint, and as a result, the trial court was without subject matter jurisdiction. The appellate court found that the operator did have judicial standing as a consequence of specific legislative mandate. The remedy under § 67-1-707 provided an unacceptable remedy for a taxpayer whose taxes were tainted with the illegality of wrongful assessments or any form of invalidity which may not be processed on an administrative basis. The operator was subrogated to whatever remedy the consumer taxpayer would have. Under the Maritime Transportation Security Act, 33 U.S.C.S. 5(b), there was a conflict between the county's local privilege tax and the statute, which prohibited the levying and collection of a tax from any vessel or water craft operating on any navigable waters subject to the authority of the United States or from its passengers or crew. The conflict was irreconcilable. Any refunds of monies belonged tot he consumers, not the operator.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment in favor of the operator was affirmed, and the trial court's orders granting the county's motion to alter or amend such summary judgment and motion to dismiss were reversed.

 

1145 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


GMC v. Tenn. Motor Vehicle Comm'n


No. M2008-00082-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 667


September 8, 2008, Session 
October 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 07-262-I. Claudia C. Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, upheld a decision by appellee Tennessee Motor Vehicle Commission (Commission) forbidding appellant vehicle manufacturer from approving a proposed relocation of appellant car dealer to Mt. Juliet from Nashville, and denying the dealer a license for the new location. The manufacturer and dealer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer and dealer argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-17-114(c)(20) (Supp. 2007) did not apply to the relocation of an existing dealership and that the Commission erroneously assigned the burden of proof to them, rather than to appellee competitor. The appellate court noted that the pertinent question was not how many franchised dealers there were, in total, but rather how many franchised dealers were in the relevant marketing area. Dealer relocations were unquestionably regulated by the statutory scheme of which § 55-17-114(c)(20) was a part. A separate license was required for each location and franchise, Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-17-110 (Supp. 2007). The Commission acted within its authority in subjecting the manufacturer and dealer to a hearing on their proposed relocation under the auspices of § 55-17-114(c)(20). The administrative law judge did not abuse the discretion granted by Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1360-4-1-.02(7) where the manufacturer and dealer sought to change the present state of affairs when they proposed to relocate the dealer. The Commission followed the statutory principles, as well as the guidelines laid down by the Tennessee Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissing their medical malpractice suit against defendants, a physician, a nurse, and two health care facilities, based on the statute of repose.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a medical malpractice action in 2007, alleging negligence preceding the birth of their daughter in 2001. Huls v. Alford


No. M2008-00408-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 633


September 9, 2008, Session 
October 22, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Coffee County. No. 06-342. Allen W. Wallace, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents sought review of an order from the Chancery Court for Coffee County (Tennessee), which granted petitioner maternal grandparents' request for visitation with their grandson under the Tennessee Grandparent Visitation Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306.


OVERVIEW: The parents were divorced. The mother was designated as their child's primary residential parent and the father received co-parenting time. The grandparents filed a petition against the parents, seeking court-ordered visitation with their grandson. The trial court granted the petition and established a visitation schedule for the grandparents. On appeal, the court found that the testimony at trial preponderated in favor of a finding that the parents did not oppose visitation. The undisputed testimony at trial by the parents was that they did not oppose visitation. Such a conclusion was reinforced by the grandparents' testimony regarding the visitation that they had as well as their admission that they chose not to exercise visitation at other times. In order for § 36-6-306 to have been implicated, visitation by the grandparents would have had to have been opposed by the parents. Because the parents did not oppose visitation, the statute was not implicated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dismissed the case.

Gann v. City of Chattanooga


No. E2007-01886-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 583


April 23, 2008, Session 
September 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 07-0069. Howell N. Peoples, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, dismissed plaintiff residents' declaratory judgment action against defendants, city, city council, and developer, finding that the residents had failed to prove that the zoning decision lacked a rational basis or was arbitrary, capricious or unconstitutional. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the residents' contention that the trial court erred by utilizing the wrong burden of proof lacked merit. The law deliberately made the residents' burden high, out of deference to the legislative power over zoning matters. The trial court specifically found that there was no arbitrary, capricious or unconstitutional action on the part of the city council. The residents did not prove that the city council erroneously believed their rezoning action was in compliance with the Hixson-North River Land Use Plan (Land Use Plan). The council was allowed to deviate from the plan. The record did not demonstrate that the different results in 2002 and 2006 constituted either discrimination or arbitrary inconsistency. The decision to rezone was debated by the city council and a rational basis existed for the council's decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Universal Outdoor, Inc. v. Tenn. DOT


No. M2006-02212-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 558


September 7, 2007, Session 
September 24, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-887-IV. Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, affirmed the decision of the administrative law judge (ALJ) ordering appellant owner's long-existing billboard to be removed to permit the expansion of a highway right-of-way. Appellee Tennessee Department of Transportation (Department) refused to renew the permit for the sign or issue a new permit because its new location was improper. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department argued that the new location did not comply with the requirements of the Tennessee Billboard Regulation and Control Act of 1972, Tenn. Code Ann. § 54-21-101 et seq. (Tennessee Act), which was enacted in response to the Federal Highway Beautification Act of 1965, 23 U.S.C.S §§ 131, 136 and 319. The appellate court noted that the Department's decision to deny the permits required by the owner and to order the removal of its billboard was consistent with the Tennessee Act and the regulations promulgated under it. The owner violated the prohibitions in the rules against changing the location of the sign and replacing poles, posts or support structures. The new sign was prohibited by Tenn. Code Ann. § 54-21-104(a) and did not qualify under the rule for pre-existing signs. The owner was not entitled to the protection or benefits of Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208 as it was governed by the Tennessee Act and any relief had to arise from the Tennessee Act or the rules promulgated pursuant to it. The State's action did not amount to a "taking" of the owner's property in violation of the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution or Tennessee Constitution in Article I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, dismissed plaintiff residents' complaint seeking the removal of defendants, Knox County officials, from office on the ground that they were ineligible for their positions by operation of the term limits provision of the Knox County Charter. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The residents argued that the trial court erred in dismissing their action because it had been rendered moot by the Tennessee Supreme Court's decision in another case and subsequent events including the election and installation of new Knox County officials in the positions of those challenged. The appellate court found that all of the issues raised by the complaint were now moot, in light of the facts that all of the officials that the action sought to have removed no longer held officer, their replacements had been ostensibly duly elected, and the supreme court had held that the officials found to be term-limited in the other case legitimately held office as de facto officers until their successors were named in accordance with law. The successors had been named, elected, and inaugurated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. DeSelm v. Knox County


No. E2007-00913-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 491


June 16, 2008, Session 
August 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State & Knox County ex rel. Deselm v. Knox County, 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 519 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 166797-2. Daryl R. Fansler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff-appellants, the state and county through relators, appealed from an order of the Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee), in favor of defendant-appellee, the county election commission, that it had no declaratory judgment authority to order new elections, that the claims seeking new elections were otherwise moot, that the validity of the charter was moot, and in the alternative, that the plaintiffs lacked standing.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted a home rule charter which included term limits for elected office holders. The Tennessee Attorney General (AG) opined that the term-limit provisions were unconstitutional, and the county's officials proceeded on the assumption that the term limits were ineffective. A court opinion cast doubt upon the AG opinion. The relators sued, seeking a declaratory judgment to enforce the term limits in the charter. The county commissioners, who stood to be disqualified if the charter and thus the term limits were to be ruled valid, sought to have the charter declared invalid. The trial court had properly found the issue of the validity of the county charter to be moot. Eight possibly term-limited county commissioners and a sheriff, county clerk, register of deeds, and trustee were reelected in 2006. The relators attempted to amend the complaint and to negate those election results, an issue which had also already been settled by other litigation. The validity of the 2006 election was at least moot with regard to the issues that are actually discussed in the record. Amendment of the relators' complaint would also have been futile.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Costs on appeal were taxed to the relators, and the case was remanded to the trial court for collection of costs assessed.

Appeal granted by Smith County Reg'l Planning Comm'n v. Hiwassee Vill. Mobile Home Park, LLC, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 601 (Tenn., May 4, 2009)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Smith County Reg'l Planning Comm'n v. Hiwassee Vill. Mobile Home Park, LLC, 304 S.W.3d 302, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 30 (Tenn., Jan. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Smith County. No. 5013-W. John Wootten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee planning commission sought civil penalties and injunctive relief against appellant mobile home park alleged to be in violation of a private act regulating mobile home parks in the county. The Circuit Court for Smith County, Tennessee, found that the mobile home park was not protected by a grandfather provision and ordered injunctive relief to bring the mobile home park into compliance with the private act. The mobile home park appealed.


OVERVIEW: In November 1997, two brothers quit claimed their interest in the subject property to an owner who intended to establish a mobile home park. In July 1997, the planning commission circulated to its members a proposed private act to regulate mobile home parks. On May 11, 1998, the act took effect. Prior to this date, the owner had taken substantial steps to operate the mobile home park. He have even collected collecting rent for the mobile home park lots. The trial court erred in finding that the owner failed to carry his burden of proof to show the mobile home park was in operation before the act took effect. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee held that mobile home park was classified as a residential use; therefore, it was not subject to the grandfather protection of Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208(b)(1). The trial court did not err by finding that the mobile home park was abandoned. For more than one year, the property deteriorated to the point where there was no administrative control and people were living there without paying any rent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re J.B.


No. E2007-01467-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 376


March 20, 2008, Session 
June 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. Nos. 1. Timothy E. Irwin, Judge


1 This is a consolidated appeal of eleven juvenile court cases. The "complaint numbers" in those cases were Nos. 30748, 30749, 30753, 30754, 30755, 30756, 30757, 30758, 30759, 30761 and 30762.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state brought suit against appellee county and appellee city before a chancery court seeking reimbursement for costs associated with the mental health evaluations of juveniles. The chancery court ordered the state to seek relief from the Juvenile Court for Knox County, Tennessee. The juvenile court issued separate orders. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three juveniles were charged with offenses that would have been felonies if the juveniles had been adults. The other eight juveniles were charged with misdemeanors. The county and the state disputed which governmental entity should pay for costs associated with the mental evaluations of the eleven juveniles. The state argued for the enforcement of a distinction between direct and incidental costs. Nevertheless, the state failed at the trial court level to make the statutory distinction it advanced on appeal. The juvenile court based its judgments in significant part on the notion an expense for the care of each child was an incidental cost, governed by Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-150(b). The appellate court had no way of knowing whether the amount charged to the state in the three felony cases was based entirely on cost of the examination. The appellate court concluded that the fairest course was to leave the trial court's determination undisturbed with respect to the three juveniles charged with felony offenses. With respect to a juvenile charged with a misdemeanor, there was no statutory authorization for charging the state with the costs. The county was responsible for the costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed with respect to orders requiring the county to pay costs in misdemeanor cases. The orders requiring the state to pay the costs of juveniles that were charged with felonies were also affirmed. The order requiring the state to pay the costs associated with a juvenile who was charged with a misdemeanor was reversed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for enforcement of the judgment as modified.

Waters v. Ray


No. M2006-01453-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

June 25, 2008, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-2083-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted respondent warden's motion to dismiss and awarded summary judgment to respondent Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Correction on petitioner inmate's declaratory judgment alleging Tennessee Code Annotated § 40-25-143 had been unconstitutionally retroactively applied to his inmate trust account to reimburse the State for costs arising from his prosecution. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that, despite its August 2006 order vacating the trial court's order dismissing the inmate's Rule 59 motion for lack of jurisdiction and remanding the matter to the trial court for adjudication of the motion, the trial court's September 2006 order merely reiterated its earlier order dismissing on the basis of lack of jurisdiction. Pursuant to Tenn. R. App. P. 4(e), the inmate filed a premature notice of appeal where he filed the notice after filing a Rule 59 motion to alter or amend but before the trial court had adjudicated that motion. Accordingly, the trial court retained jurisdiction over the inmate's timely-filed Rule 59 motion. Because the inmate had filed his notice of appeal, jurisdiction would vest in the appellate court when the trial court entered a final order adjudicating the motion on its merits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded to the trial court with instructions to comply with the appellate court's order of August 30, 2006, and dispose of the motion on its merits.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee maternal grandmother filed a petition seeking visitation pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-6-306 and 36-6-307 (2001). The Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granted the petition and awarded the grandmother 78 days of visitation annually. Appellant father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother provided housing and served as a primary caregiver for the child when the child and the mother moved to Tennessee. The mother died when the child was five years old. However, the visitation schedule required remand.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed in part the trial court's judgment as to a portion of the visitation schedule and the injunctions against non-parties, affirmed the judgment as to the remaining issues, and assessed the costs of appeal against the father.

Hayes v. Gibson County


No. W2007-01849-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 244


February 21, 2008, Session 
April 29, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 29, 2008.
Reversed by, Remanded by Hayes v. Gibson County, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 321 (Tenn., July 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Gibson County. No. 18296. Roy B. Morgan, Judge Sitting by Interchange.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee clerk sought a declaration of his rights under Tennessee Code Annotated § 8-24-102 as amended in 2001, asserting that the 2001 amendments repealed by implication 2000 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 142, establishing the compensation of appellant County's juvenile court clerk. The Chancery Court for Gibson County, Tennessee, determined the amendments superseded the private act and awarded the clerk back pay. The County appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the County contended the trial court erred in ruling that the general law as opposed to the private act was applicable to the issue of which salary act should have been used to calculate the clerk's salary in his capacity as the county juvenile court clerk. In light of the general assembly's presumed knowledge of the provisions of the general statute when it enacted 2000 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 142, and in light of its presumed awareness of the private act when it amended the general provisions of section 8-24-102 in 2001, coupled with the absence of any language in the 2001 amendments to Tennessee Code Annotated § 8-24-102 repealing this or any similar private act, the appellate court held that the 2001 amendments to Tennessee Code Annotated § 8-24-102 did not repeal 2000 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 142 by implication. Additionally, the private act was not blatantly unconstitutional on its face, and the issue of whether it was unconstitutional under Tennessee Code Annotated § 8-24-102 was not properly raised in the trial court where the Attorney General was not served with notice of this litigation. As such, the trial court erred in ruling in favor of the clerk.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a child's aunt and uncle and the prospective adoptive parents, appealed the judgment of the Juvenile Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) that dismissed their petition for termination of appellee father's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners argued, inter alia, that the evidence clearly and convincingly established that the father abandoned the child. The court of appeals agreed. It was undisputed that the father did not visit or support the child during the four month period leading up to August 16, 2005, the date of the termination petition. The father had not seen the child since the mother left the father after Christmas of 2003, and the father never sent financial support or gifts to the child while he lived with the great aunt. However, the father argued that his failure to visit or support the child was not willful because the great aunt interfered with his visitation. However, the father did nothing to attempt to maintain even minimal contact with the child through a card, letter, or gift. The father testified that the great aunt let him speak to the child twice in February of 2004, yet the father did not attempt to call the child again after that month. Therefore, the trial court erred by failing to terminate the father's parental rights on the ground of abandonment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

December 5, 2007, Assigned on Briefs

Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 07-79-IV. Richard Dinkins, Chancellor.
Meeks v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1231 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was denied parole by appellee Tennessee Board of Probation and Parole and lost his administrative appeal. The court clerk returned his petition for writ of certiorari because he owed court costs from previous litigation. The court costs were paid, and the inmate was allowed to file his petition. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, subsequently dismissed the petition as not being timely filed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended the 60-day statute of limitations under Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-9-102 was tolled when he submitted the complaint until the clerk's office notified him that his prior court costs were paid; Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-812 was unconstitutional; and the trial court erred in assessing court costs against him. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that when the petition was resubmitted and filed, the mandatory 60-day filing period had expired, and the trial court did not have jurisdiction to hear the case; the limitations statute made no provision for tolling. Since the inmate did not raise the constitutionality of § 41-21-812 issue at trial and it was not unconstitutional on its face, the appellate court would not entertain the issue on appeal. As the Board was the prevailing party and no extraordinary circumstances warranting review appeared in the record, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in assessing court costs against the inmate under Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-12-119.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Flautt & Mann v. Council of Memphis


No. W2006-02227-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


285 S.W.3d 856; 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 84


October 12, 2007, Session 
February 20, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. 75359-4. T.D. Rita L. Stotts, Judge.
Flautt & Mann v. Council of the City of Memphis, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 235 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 22, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city council and a city, challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which, on remand, found that the city was in willful contempt of a prior order relating to a zoning application filed appellee landowners and assessed daily damages accruing from the date of the prior order until there was compliance with the order.


OVERVIEW: The landowners sought to change the zoning on a parcel of land from agricultural to commercial. After several procedural steps in the case, the trial court found that willful contempt existed due to the council's failure to comply with a prior order. Daily damages were assessed. This appeal followed. In vacating, the appellate court rejected the assertion that there could have been no finding of contempt; a prior order of the trial court was not void based on a lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Even though zoning ordinances were legislative acts, the trial court did have authority over such. The trial court properly treated the landowners' action as one for a declaratory judgment and proceeded accordingly. Next, the appellate court had jurisdiction to review the contempt finding, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-4-108(b) (1994). Even if the trial court's order regarding the new hearing might have been improper, disobeying such was not the proper decision. The council improperly entertained new evidence at the hearing. However, the trial court's use of a coercive fine was improper because it was awarded retroactively prior to the finding of contempt.


OUTCOME: The decision was vacated. The case was remanded to the council for a new hearing. The hearing was ordered to follow the proper procedure; it should have provided a proper notice and a hearing, and it should have considered current information.

 

1160 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Free the Fathers, Inc. v. State


No. M2006-02329-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 67


August 10, 2007, Session 
February 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Free the Fathers, Inc. v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 438 (Tenn., June 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-2073. III Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, affirmed the decision of appellee, Charitable Solicitations Division of the Tennessee Department of State (State), enjoining appellant not-for-profit charitable corporation from soliciting charitable funds. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the chancellor erred in interpreting the Solicitation of Charitable Funds Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-101-501, et. seq., as to its application to the corporation. It argued that the Act violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution, the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution, and Article 1, Section 3 of the Tennessee Constitution. The appellate court found that the corporation failed to fulfill a condition precedent to being eligible for either exemption under the Act. It never submitted the form prescribed by the secretary of state, and it never provided the statutorily mandated information. The Act did not impose a constitutionally impermissible prior restraint as it did not envision a grant or denial of a license or a permit, only registration. The State did not have the discretion to deny registration. The corporation failed to support its contention that the Act violated the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The corporation failed to establish that it had standing for a Commerce Clause claim. The Act did not violate Article I, Section 3 of the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wharton v. Wharton


No. W2007-01972-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 64


January 25, 2008, Session 
February 6, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Crockett County. No. 8167. George R. Ellis, Chancellor.
Wharton v. Wharton, 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 753 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 29, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Crockett County (Tennessee), which denied her request to transfer appellee father's petition for contempt to enforce a child support order.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced in Crockett County, Tennessee; however, they resided in Dyer County, Tennessee, at the time of the divorce. The mother then moved to Kentucky. The parties first shared custody of their minor child; however, the father was later designated the primary residential parent. The father later sought to enforce a child support order entered in Crockett County. The mother's request to transfer the case to Dyer County was denied, and this appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court held that the father's constitutional arguments were not preserved for review because he did not raise them before the trial court. The father did not have permission to raise such challenges in this interlocutory appeal under Rule 9 of the Rules of Appellate Procedure. Next, Tennessee Code Annotated § 36-5-3003 (2005) did not limit standing to request a transfer to the custodial parent or to residents of Tennessee. Moreover, a transfer was mandatory here because the requirements of Tennessee Code Annotated § 36-5-3003(b) (2005) were met. Finally, there was no limitation on transfers for cases where the original order was entered, despite a waiver of venue.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, the case was remanded, and the matter was ordered transferred.

 

1162 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


H & R Block E. Tax Servs. v. Dep't of Commerce & Industry, Div. of Ins.


No. M2007-00656-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


267 S.W.3d 848; 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 53


December 10, 2007, Session 
January 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by H & R Block E. Tax Servs. v. Dep't of Commerce & Ins., 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 639 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-3175-I. Claudia Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, upheld appellee Tennessee Department of Commerce and Insurance's (State) contention that appellant tax service's "Peace of Mind" (POM) program was a contract of insurance under T.C.A. § 56-7-101 as it was written, and, therefore, the tax service was subject to various penalties under that statute because it was not licensed to sell insurance. The tax service appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the threshold question for it to answer was whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-7-101(a) was devoid of ambiguity. It found that the statute did not specify what types of interest were "insurable," which was critical in determining what constituted "insurance." In light of the circular reference to "insurance" and "insurable interest," the statute implicitly incorporated some commonsense notion of what sort of contract could constitute insurance, and therefore it could not have been the legislature's intent to include such contracts as simple product warranties offered by a retailer, which did not pass such a commonsense test. The question was whether the contract, as a whole, was primarily a service guarantee or a promise of indemnity. The POM program fell on the "service" side of the service-indemnity test not because the service provided its customers with the "service" of legal representation if they were audited, but the program was that of a tax-preparation service with an added guarantee. An error by the tax service did not create an insurable "loss," but simply an unfulfilled expectation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the trial court.

Dean v. Turner


No. W2007-00744-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 773


July 31, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
December 18, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Vacated and the Appeal is Dismissed for Lack of Subject Matter Jurisdiction. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hardeman County. No. 15966. J. Weber McCraw, Judge.
State v. Dean, 76 S.W.3d 352, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 791 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is Vacated and the Appeal is Dismissed for Lack of Subject Matter Jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Hardeman County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of aggravated rape, and he was sentenced to 40 years of incarceration. After unsuccessfully appealing, the prisoner then filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the chancery court. It dismissed the petition, and this appeal followed. In vacating, the appellate court determined that the chancery court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over this case, pursuant to Tenn. R. App. P. 13(b). Despite the language in T.C.A. § 29-21-103 (2000) referencing chancellors, they had no authority to inquire into the restraint of prisoners or the validity of criminal convictions. The language of the statute referencing chancellors merely referred to restraints not criminally imposed or sanctioned. The requirement that a habeas corpus petition should have been made to the most convenient court or judge had to be read in conjunction with the limitation on the chancery court's jurisdiction. The prisoner should have sought relief from the most convenient court authorized to grant such. Thus, the petition was dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the petition was dismissed.

Hill v. Hill

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed and the Cause is Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the Chancery Court for Bedford County (Tennessee), which denied the father's motion, filed against respondent mother, to modify the father's child support obligation because he did not meet, under Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1240-2-4-.05(2)(a), the variance requirement.


OVERVIEW: The father sought a reduction in his child support obligation. Because the father had not established a significant variance of at least 15 percent under Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1240-2-4-.05(2)(a), the trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed on appeal. The father was required to show at least a 15 percent difference in his gross income from the time that child support was originally ordered until the time that he filed his modification motion. The court found no error in the trial court's decision to decline to use a case law formula to reverse engineer the father's gross income at the time of the divorce petition for purposes of determining whether a significant variance had been established. There being no transcript or statement of the evidence, for purposes of Rule 24 of the Tennessee Rules of Appellate Procedure, the court presumed that the trial court was correct in including a certain amount in the father's 2004 gross income for comparison purposes. Considering the mother's income and the outcome of the appeal, the court remanded for a determination of attorney fees under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(c) for this appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded for a determination of the mother's reasonable attorney fees on appeal.

In re Adoption of M.P.J.


No. W2007-00379-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 724


July 31, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
November 28, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Gibson County (Trenton). No. 8144. layburn Peeples, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Gibson County (Tennessee) terminating his parental rights to his child on the ground that he abandoned the child under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(1) and granting the child's great-aunts petition for adoption.


OVERVIEW: The child was removed from her mother's home when she was seven months old and placed in her great-aunt's custody. At the time, the father's whereabouts were unknown and he subsequently began serving a 56-month sentence in federal prison. When the child turned five, her great-aunt petitioned to terminate the father's parental rights and to adopt her. On appeal of the trial court's decision granting the petition, the court held that the proof clearly and convincingly established that the father abandoned the child because: (1) he only engaged in token visits with the child, as he only visited her twice in the four months before he went to prison; (2) he did not seek visitation through the trial court; (3) he testified that he had not been a good father and that the child did not know him; (4) the father admitted that he personally had not given the child any birthday or Christmas gifts prior to his incarceration; and (5) the child's great-aunt did not vigorously resist the father's to visit the child, but rather the father willfully failed to visit. Because the child's great-aunt took custody of her the Department of Children's Services was not required to attempt reunification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissing his petition for a common law writ of certiorari under Tennessee Rule of Civil Procedure 12.02(6) for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of rape and sentenced as a habitual offender to life in prison. He petition for certiorari relief, arguing that the parole board acted arbitrarily and illegally in denying him parole. On appeal, the court held that it appeared that the inmate's petition was not timely filed, because the Board's made its decision to deny him parole on July 21, 2005 but he did not file his petition for a writ of certiorari until January 27, 2006, more than 60 days after the Board's decision, which was required under Tennessee Code Annotated section 27-9-102. The court further held that the petition was properly dismissed because it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The court found no error in the Board's procedure because there was no basis to the inmate's argument that the full panel should conduct the hearing, given section 40-28-105(d)(2), and the inmate admitted that all board members declined him for parole release. The court rejected the inmate's claim that he should have been released on parole pursuant to his plea agreement because he failed to present any evidence of an alleged agreement to be paroled upon serving 30 percent of 30 years.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the inmate's petition was affirmed.

Highwoods Props. v. City of Memphis


No. W2007-00454-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 723


July 18, 2007, Session 
November 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Highwoods Props., Inc. v. City of Memphis, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 487 (Tenn., July 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-06-2070-1. Walter L. Evans, Chancellor.
Highwoods Props. v. City of Memphis, 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 789 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant properly owners challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) granting appellee city's motion to dismiss, filed under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6), in the property owners' action seeking a declaration that appellee city's annexation ordinance accomplished through a consent order was procedurally invalid and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that it had no power to vacate the annexation ordinance on the purely procedural grounds alleged by the property owners, namely that it was invalid because it was modified and/or partially repealed by a consent judgment entered in a prior quo warranto action without compliance with statutory procedures including notice and passage by the city council. The court further held that while Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-101, et seq, did not preclude the property owners from alleging constitutional violations caused by the annexation, it was apparent that the annexation ordinance did not implement an unconstitutional taxing structure, and therefore the property owners' declaratory judgment was properly dismissed. The property owners' complaint that they were forced to pay city taxes for a longer period than other property owners, whose land was not yet part of the city, did not implicate the equal and uniform clause of Article 2 § 28 of the Tennessee Constitution because, there was nothing in the record to suggest that the city or any other taxing authority was implementing different tax rates within its own borders.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the property owners' action was affirmed.

Williams v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for a writ of certiorari to challenge a denial of parole by appellee Tennessee Board of Probation and Parole.


OVERVIEW: In 1982, the inmate entered a guilty plea to robbery by use of a deadly weapon and murder during the perpetration of a robbery. Parole was denied for a second time in 2005, and the inmate filed a petition for a writ of certiorari after an administrative appeal was unsuccessful. A motion to dismiss the case was granted, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court rejected the inmate's argument that the use of the current rules and statutes relating to parole violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 11, U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10. Finally, the inmate merely offered conclusory references in attacking the board's decision; he did not show any procedural irregularities or establish that it acted illegally, fraudulently, or arbitrarily.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Waters v. Chumley


No. E2006-02225-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 570


August 15, 2007, Session 
September 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Waters v. Chumley, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 23 (Tenn., Jan. 28, 2008)
Affirmed by Waters v. Farr, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 361 (Tenn., July 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Loudon County. No. 10710. Frank V. Williams III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer was arrested for possession of cocaine. The Tennessee Department of Revenue assessed taxes, a penalty, and interest against the taxpayer under Tennessee's Drug Tax, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2801 et seq. The taxpayer filed suit against defendant Commissioner of Revenue, charging that the Drug Tax was unconstitutional. The Chancery Court for Loudon County, Tennessee, entered judgment for the taxpayer. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Drug Tax was purportedly an excise upon a particular privilege, assessed according to the quantity of substance possessed in enjoyment of such privilege. The power to tax privileges was not subject to any constitutional limitation except that the tax levied must not be arbitrary, capricious, or wholly unreasonable. The Drug Tax levied a tax on unauthorized substances and specifically provided that the tax did not apply to a substance in the possession of a dealer who was authorized by law to possess the substance, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2804(a). Furthermore, the tax applied only to persons in unauthorized possession of substances which the legislature declared to be illegal. Because it sought to levy a tax on the privilege to engage in an activity that the legislature previously declared to be a crime, not a privilege, the court found that the Drug Tax was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable, and therefore, invalid under the Constitution of Tennessee. The legislature's enactment of the Drug Tax was not supported by the rationale justifying the enactment of a privilege tax.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hankins v. Hankins


No. W2006-00232-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 533


April 18, 2007, Session 
August 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hankins v. Hankins, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 48 (Tenn., Feb. 4, 2008)
Costs and fees proceeding at Hankins v. Hankins, 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 216 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-007025-03. John R. McCarroll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the wife, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which found in favor of defendant, the husband, and found that the marriage was invalid because her service of process on her second husband during her second divorce had been insufficient. The circuit court also distributed property and made an alimony award to the wife during the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed for divorce from her husband and the husband collaterally attacked the validity of the wife's previous divorce from her second husband. The trial court found that the wife's efforts at service of process on her second husband during her second divorce had been insufficient, and ruled that any subsequent marriage was therefore invalid. The trial court also found that a bank account held jointly by the parties was the sole property of the husband, and it awarded each party a one-half interest in real property located in Tennessee. The appellate court reversed in part, stating that the trial court's allowance of a collateral attack by the husband on the issue of jurisdiction was in contravention of the law as his basis for such attack was, in part, parole proof, and not a facially void decree. The trial court erred in finding that the marriage was void ab initio and erred in applying the Falk standards for property division since the marriage was valid and not void from its inception. The award of alimony, however, was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held that the trial court erred by permitting the husband to collaterally attack the prior divorce decree, reversed the judgment as to the division of property, affirmed the award of alimony, and remanded for further proceedings as to the parties' respective claims for divorce and for further proceedings as to their claims for the distribution of property.

JPMorgan Chase Bank v. Franklin Nat'l Bank


No. M2005-02088-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 522


August 15, 2006, Session 
August 13, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 29966. Russ Heldman, Judge.
JPMorgan Chase Bank v. Fifth Third Bank, N.A., 222 Fed. Appx. 444, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 285 (6th Cir. Tenn., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter arose from a dispute between plaintiff bank and defendant bank regarding plaintiff's liability for discretionary costs after voluntarily dismissing the complaint it had filed against defendant in the Chancery Court for Williamson County, Tennessee. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following the entry of a voluntary dismissal, defendant, invoking Tenn. R. Civ. P. 41.04 and 54.04, requested the trial court to award its attorney's fees and court reporter expenses as discretionary costs. On appeal, plaintiff took issue with the award of discretionary costs and requested a declaration that defendant violated Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11 by requesting these costs. The trial court did err by awarding defendant its attorney's fees as discretionary costs, but the trial did not abuse its discretion in awarding court reporter expenses. The trial court lacked jurisdiction to award costs under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 41.04 because plaintiff did not commence its subsequent action in the chancery court, but it instead commenced the action in the federal court. Even if the appellate court assumed, arguendo, that Tenn. R. Civ. P. 41.04 allowed trial courts to award attorney's fees following the voluntary dismissal of a case as part of the costs of the action previously dismissed, the appellate court would still find the trial court erred by awarding attorney's fees in this case. The appellate court also declined to consider whether defendant's conduct violated Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the portion of the order with respect to fees, and it remanded the case to the trial court with directions to reduce the judgment and for whatever further proceedings consistent with the rule as was required.

McMahan v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1]

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granting summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Tennessee Department of Correction (TDOC), dismissing the inmate's declaratory judgment suit asserting that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-123 violated his constitutional rights of due process and constituted double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: In 1989, the inmate was convicted of various drug-related offenses, and was sentenced to a 42 years of imprisonment with parole eligibility after serving 30 percent of that sentence. The inmate was assigned to a county work camp, where he was assigned a position as park worker and was allowed to work in the community. In 1992, while imprisoned at the county work camp, the inmate was convicted of possession of contraband, a felony. Based on this conviction and pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-123(b)(1), the inmate lost his parole eligibility date. The appellate court ruled that the inmate's constitutional rights were not violated. Because Tennessee did not recognize a constitutional right to early release, the inmate could not show that he had suffered a deprivation of a liberty interest or that he was entitled to any procedural due process in the TDOC's revocation of his release eligibility date. Also, the inmate failed to provide any evidence or cite any authorities in support of his contention that his equal protection rights were violated in any way.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1176 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


County of Shelby v. Tompkins


No. W2006-01433-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


241 S.W.3d 500; 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 433


January 10, 2007, Assigned on Brief 
July 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by County of Shelby v. Tompkins, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 1071 (Tenn., Nov. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County No. CH-04-1691-3. D.J. Alissandratos, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county fire department terminated appellant firefighter's employment for a conceded violation of the county residency requirement set forth in Shelby County, Tenn., Charter § 5.10. The county civil service merit board modified the department's sanction from termination to suspension without pay. On appeal, the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) reinstated the department's termination. The firefighter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The firefighter argued that the charter did not mandate termination; that, even if it did, he had moved back to Shelby County at the time of his termination and should not have been discharged; and that, alternatively, he was entitled to a remand to advance an equal protection argument because he was unfairly prevented from doing so in the lower court. The court of appeals agreed with the trial court that § 5.10 (C) was "clear in and of itself" and held that the charter provision mandated only one sanction for the violation. Because the charter residency requirement mandated the termination of employment when an individual had violated it, the merit board exceeded its authority when, in contravention of that provision, it modified the firefighter's sanction from termination to suspension without pay. There was no dispute that the firefighter resided in another county at the time the department filed charges against him. Given that fact, his subsequent attempt to cure the violation was ineffectual. Moreover, the firefighter had waived the equal protection issue by failing to raise it in the lower court; the court of appeals therefore denied his request for a remand.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The case was remanded. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the firefighter and his surety, for which execution could issue if necessary.

Lay v. Comm'r, Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2005-02245-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 426


June 5, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
July 10, 2007, Filed on


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 03-3423-IV. Richard Dinkins, Chancellor.
Lay v. State, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 233 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 19, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed petitioner inmate's declaratory judgment action in which he challenged the constitutionality of an amendment to Tennessee's statutory scheme governing parole eligibility. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the 1998 enactment of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-28-115(h)(2) and 40-35-501(i)(2) and their application to him constituted a violation of several vested rights. The appellate court found that the statutes did not have the effect of delaying the inmate's first parole eligibility hearing. The inmate's initial release eligibility date was in 1997, and pursuant to that eligibility, he was afforded a parole hearing on June 24, 1997. The parole board denied him parole at that time. The inmate's assertion that he acquired a liberty interest in being paroled was without merit. The amendment to the statutes did not constitute an illegal pronouncement of guilt by the legislature. The inmate was challenging the validity of the statute, not the validity of the policy. The legislature's defining of the factors the Board of Probation and Parole had to consider in making a decision about whether to afford an inmate a parole hearing did not encroach upon the Board or the executive branch. The amendment to the statutes did not constitute a sentence enhancement scheme because no time was added to the inmate's sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Smith County v. Enoch

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Smith County, Tennessee, issued a permanent injunction against appellant, the operator of an automobile junkyard, enjoining him from maintaining an excessive number of inoperable vehicles within one thousand feet of a county road. The operator appealed.

Colonial Pipeline Co. v. Morgan


No. M2006-00591-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 408


April 10, 2007, Session 
July 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, Remanded by Colonial Pipeline Co. v. Morgan, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 589 (Tenn., Sept. 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-748-IV. Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed appellant carrier's constitutional challenges to portions of Tennessee's tax system. The trial court dismissed the complaint on the basis that the carrier failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. The carrier appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State argued that the carrier's action against the State could not be maintained because the carrier failed to exhaust its administrative remedies and a petition for declaratory judgment could not be maintained against the State. The appellate court found that the carrier was seeking a declaratory judgment that the present tax scheme was unconstitutional. It was permissible for the carrier to commence and maintain the declaratory judgment action. The carrier's issues concerned legal challenges to the statutory scheme. Where a party's complaint raised primarily questions of law, the court was the appropriate body to adjudicate the issues, and, therefore, the complaining party was not required to exhaust its administrative remedies. The carrier's facial challenge to the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-501(9)(B)(iii) could not be determined by an administrative tribunal in an administrative proceeding. Requiring that the carrier return to the State Board of Equalization would not give the Board an opportunity to correct an error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the chancery court.

Tenn. Dep't of Human Servs. v. Priest Lake Cmty. Baptist Church


No. M2006-00302-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 391


March 7, 2007, Session 
June 25, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-1469-I. Claudia Bonnyman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted judgment in favor of appellee Tennessee Department of Human Services (DHS) by entering a permanent injunction against appellant church preventing it from operating its Bible School unless or until it obtained a license. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that because the church was providing "child care," in the sense that its staff supervised, protected, and met basic needs, for at least 13 children for more than 3 hours per day, the church's Bible School met the definition of a "child care center" under Tennessee's child care licensing laws. The concerns expressed by the church did not demonstrate that it had suffered an injury in factor or that it faced immediate injury from enforcement of the day care licensing regulations. The child care licensing laws clearly regulated conduct, not one's beliefs. Any finding that the Bible School ministry was a religious activity in and of itself would not have exempted the church from the state licensing requirement. The licensing statute did not textually discriminate against religion or religious groups. There was no indication that DHS was routinely making subjective assessments of a program's justification for providing child care that would present the opportunity for religious discrimination. The licensing law need not be justified by a compelling governmental interest even if it had the incidental effect of burdening the church's religious practice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johns v. Dalton

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

King v. Tenn. Bd. of Paroles


No. M2005-02821-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 346


April 2, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 1


1 This appeal was assigned to this panel on.

 
May 29, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-114-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.
King v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 648 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 24, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After unsuccessfully appealing a parole denial administratively, appellant petitioner filed a petition for writ of certiorari claiming that appellee board of paroles improperly applied a version of the statute governing parole of sex offenders which was amended after he committed the crimes. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) determined there was no ex post facto violation and dismissed the petition. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner claimed that the version of the statute as it existed when he committed the crimes should have been applied and application of the statute as amended resulted in an ex post facto violation. The petitioner claimed that he was denied due process and that the board's application of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-116 violated the constitutional prohibition on ex post facto laws. The issue was whether application of § 40-28-116, as amended after the petitioner committed the crimes, was disadvantageous to him. The appellate court held that the petitioner had not demonstrated that application of the amended statute would in any way effectively postpone his initial release date. Moreover, his claim that application of the amended statute would postpone his release date was nothing more than pure speculation. The amended statute was less restrictive than the statute in effect at the time the petitioner committed the aggravated rape in 1981. Therefore, there was no impermissible ex post facto violation. The petitioner's due process claim was equally without merit. There was ample material evidence to support the board's findings and the trial court properly dismissed the petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court for collection of the costs below. Costs on appeal were taxed to the petitioner.

Sons of Confederate Veterans, Inc. v. Sweeney

April 16, 2007, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Maury County. No. 05-092. Robert L. Jones, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit corporation members sued defendant corporate officer, seeking injunctive relief prohibiting the officer from acting in his former capacity. The Chancery Court for Maury County (Tennessee) found that the members were not properly before the court because of defects in the initial complaint, allowed them to intervene, and awarded them attorneys' fees under Miss. Code Ann. § 79-11-193 (2005). The officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that the members had met the demand requirement of Miss. Code Ann. § 79-11-193 (2005) because although their initial complaint contained no allegations of a demand upon the corporation, their subsequent motion to intervene was properly granted under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 24.02 (2006) and they were properly allowed to file an amended complaint. Moreover, based on the officer's failure to include a transcript of evidence, the appellate court presumed that the evidence presented at multiple hearings supported the trial court's finding that the corporation's executive council refused to appropriately respond to the members' objections before and after the litigation was instituted. Thus, the trial court properly awarded the members attorneys' fees. The officer also failed to provide any authority for his argument that the members lacked standing to bring an action on behalf of the corporation based upon the corporate bylaws. That argument appeared to be founded upon the members' alleged failure to satisfy the Mississippi statute, an argument the appellate court had already rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment awarding the members attorneys' fees was affirmed.

McNiel v. Cooper


No. M2005-01206-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


241 S.W.3d 886; 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 241


April 5, 2006, Session  
March 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McNiel v. Cooper, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 728 (Tenn., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-1748-IV. Richard Dinkins, Chancellor.
McNiel v. Cooper, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 134 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, concluded that appellee physician received adequate notice of the purpose of the request for medical records by appellant Tennessee Board of Medical Examiners (Board) and determined that Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-117(a)(3) was unconstitutional and awarded the physician $20,916 in attorney's fees. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that the Board and the Division of Health Related Boards (Division) in the Tennessee Department of Health (Department) had concurrent authority to enforce compliance with the laws regulating the practice of medicine in Tennessee in order to prevent unlawful practices. The Division and Board had statutory authority to license and oversee the professional conduct of physicians practicing in Tennessee. Physicians who complied with the Division's or Board's request for patient records did not violate the implied covenant of confidentiality because they were required to honor a proper request for patient records. The procedure mandated by Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-117(a)(3) for obtaining patient records appropriately balances the patients' privacy interests, the physicians' interest in practicing medicine free from unreasonable governmental interference, and the State's compelling interest in protecting the health and safety of its citizens. The physician received adequate information regarding the information when he was served with the request for records.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed concluding that the physician received adequate notice of the purpose of the Division's request for medical records, and the judgment was reversed concluding that the statute was unconstitutional and awarding the physician attorney fees. The judgment was remanded to the trial court with directions to dismiss the physician's complaint for declaratory judgment.

Hilloak Realty Co. v. Chumley


No. E2006-00213-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


233 S.W.3d 816; 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 170


September 19, 2006, Session  
March 29, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hilloak Realty Co. v. Chumley, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 701 (Tenn., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 161778-2. Daryl Fansler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A taxpayer sued the Commissioner of Revenue of the State of Tennessee, challenging the decision to assess the taxpayer excise taxes predicated on a transfer of an apartment complex to the mortgage holder. The Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee) held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2006(b)(2)(C) permitted the taxpayer to increase its depreciated basis, resulting in no excise taxes being due. The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the taxpayer was required to utilize its federal basis in the property in determining if it was obligated to pay state excise taxes as a result of the "sale" of the property. The trial court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2006(b)(2)(C) was not limited to situations where there was a legislatively-mandated "decoupling" of the net earnings tax basis for excise tax purposes from federal taxable income. This case was an example of one of the different ways a taxpayer could have a higher basis in property for purposes of the state excise tax laws versus federal income tax law. While the taxpayer claimed the pre-1999 depreciation deductions and its federal income tax basis was lower, it also received a clear benefit from those deductions via a reduction in its ordinary income. If the taxpayer was unable to utilize a higher basis, it received no corresponding benefit on the state side from the lowered basis. The amount of the federal basis was $ 3,913,882. The difference between that basis and the state basis was the amount of the pre-1999 depreciation deductions, $ 6,524,612. When that amount was taken into consideration, there was no income from the transaction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings and for collection of costs. Costs on appeal were assessed to the Commissioner.
