Lee v. Franklin Special Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ.


No. M2005-02716-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


237 S.W.3d 322; 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 133


October 11, 2006, Session  
March 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Lee v. Franklin Special Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ., 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 196 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 29, 2007)
Appeal denied by Lee v. Franklin Special Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ., 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 769 (Tenn., Aug. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 29621. Timothy Easter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenured teacher, whose position was abolished due to a system wide reduction in force, filed an action due to appellee school district's failure to afford her preferential consideration for reemployment pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-5-511(b)(3) of the Teacher Tenure Act. The Chancery Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) summarily dismissed the teacher's claim. The teacher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The chancery court concluded that, as a matter of law, the teacher was not entitled to preferential consideration for teaching positions that were to start after July 1, 2002, because her tenure expired due to the fact she was 65 years of age. The appellate court concluded that the teacher's right to preferential consideration vested prior to July 1, 2002, which afforded her the right to be placed and to remain on the preferred list for up to two years, until she refused a bona fide offer of reemployment for a comparable position or accepted a position, which she had not done. Moreover, since the board of education did not consider the competence or qualifications of the teacher to hold a teaching position after the reduction in force announcement, as it was statutorily entitled to do pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-5-511(b)(3), it waived the right to contend that the teacher was unqualified, incompatible, or unsuitable to hold one of the available teaching positions for which she interviewed. The appellate court therefore concluded that the teacher was entitled to reemployment for the 2002-03 school year and that she was wrongfully denied reemployment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was vacated. The case was remanded for entry of an order granting the teacher's motion for summary judgment and determination of the compensation that the teacher was entitled to receive for the 2002-03 school year. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the school district.

McNiel v. Cooper


No. M2005-01206-COA-R3-CV

2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 134


April 5, 2006, Session

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 30, 2007.
Opinion withdrawn by McNiel v. Cooper, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 195 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2007)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by McNiel v. Cooper, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 241 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-1748-IV. Richard Dinkins, Chancellor.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant Tennessee Board of Medical Examiners requested access to appellee physician's patients' records in accordance with Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-117 (2004), the physician filed a declaratory judgment action in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) challenging the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The physician asserted that the statutory procedure for gaining access to medical records amounted to an unreasonable search and seizure because it failed to provide him with pre-enforcement judicial review of the reasonableness of the Board's request. He also claimed that the statute's notice provisions violated due process. Both the physician and the Board filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court held that the physician received adequate notice of the purpose of the request for medical records. It also determined that § 63-1-117(a)(3), the portion of the statute authorizing disciplinary sanctions against physicians who willfully failed to produce requested records, was unconstitutional and awarded the physician attorney's fees. The Board appealed. The appellate court agreed that the physician received adequate notice of the reasons for the request for medical records. However, physicians in Tennessee had no reasonable expectation that they could shield their patients' records from the Board's regulatory oversight and the Board could discipline physicians who willfully refused to comply with lawful requests for patient records that comply with § 63-1-117.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment concluding that the physician received adequate notice of the purpose of the request for medical records was affirmed. The portions of the judgment concluding that § 63-1-117(a)(3) was unconstitutional and awarding the physician $ 20,916 in legal fees was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to dismiss the complaint for declaratory judgment. Costs were taxed to the physician.

In re the Adoption of J.K.W.


No. E2006-00906-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 32


September 21, 2006, Session  
January 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re J. K. W. v. Watson, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 442 (Tenn., Apr. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 05-A-050. W. Frank Brown, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) terminated appellant father's rights to his biological child because it was in the child's best interest under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(6) (2005). The father challenged the constitutionality of the statute, alleging that it was not narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest. The trial court found that the statute was constitutional. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The child was the result of his unlawful sexual relationship with his 12-year-old stepdaughter. The father was convicted of two counts of attempted child rape and sentenced to serve 10 years in prison on each count, with the sentences to be served concurrently. When the child was about four years old, the foster parents filed a petition to terminate the father's parental rights and to adopt the child. The foster parents alleged the ground set forth in § 36-1-113(g)(6) as the sole basis for terminating the father's parental rights. The statute provided for termination of a parent's rights where the parent was under a sentence of 10 or more years and the child was under eight years of age at the time the sentence was entered. The appellate court found that the statute was not blatantly or facially unconstitutional. The appellate court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(6) (2005) was not constitutionally deficient because of its failure to expressly require a separate finding that continuation of the parent-child relationship threatened the welfare of the child. Thus, the appellate court concluded that the statute was narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment terminating the father's rights to his child. The case was remanded to the trial court for enforcement of the trial court's judgment and for collection of costs.

 

1190 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Watchtower Bible & Tract Soc'y of N.Y., Inc.


No. M2004-01066-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 29


April 14, 2005, Session  
January 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Anderson v. Watchtower Bible & Tract Soc'y of N.Y., Inc., 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 469 (Tenn., May 14, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Anderson v. Bible, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10618 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a church and its leaders, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Coffee County (Tennessee) denying their motion to dismiss, filed under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(1), plaintiff former church members' complaint seeking damages associated with their expulsion from the church.


OVERVIEW: The church expelled the former church members, a husband and his wife, after the wife appeared on a national news program to talk about the church's handling of child sexual abuse allegations. Appellants moved to dismiss the action on the ground that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal of the trial court's judgment denying appellants' motion, the court held that the trial court should have dismissed all of the former church members' claims because they were barred by the First Amendment's protection of purely religious matters from interference by secular courts. The freedom of churches to determine their own membership was such a fundamentally ecclesiastical matter that the court was prohibited from adjudicating disputes over membership or expulsion. The court held that it could not determine whether the reasons appellants gave for the members' expulsion were pretextual because to do so it would necessarily have had to inquire into the correction of the expulsion decision and whether it was consistent with the church's religious doctrine and internal policies, an inquiry the court could not make under the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying appellants' motion to dismiss was reversed and the amended complaint was dismissed.

Jackson v. Shelby County Civ. Serv. Merit Bd.


No. W2006-01778-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 18


November 29, 2006, Assigned on Brief  
January 10, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-03-0159-1. Walter L. Evans, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a ruling from the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied his appeal under a writ of certiorari arising from appellee Shelby County Civil Service Merit Board's decision to terminate his employment with a criminal court clerk's office.


OVERVIEW: The employee put out signs during an election that opposed a clerk, an elected official. The signs implied that the clerk was a member of the Ku Klux Klan (KKK). The employee admitted in a press conference that he did not think that the clerk was a member of the KKK. The employee was informed that the signs could have been violative of Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-19-142. The Board upheld the employee's later termination for disseminating these signs. He unsuccessfully sought review under a writ of certiorari, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-8-101 (2000). This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the press conference held by the employee was not the kind prohibited by Directive 1-8 of the Criminal Court's Clerk's Administrative Manual. However, he was not terminated for violating this, but for making and distributing the political signs. The argument that Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-19-142 was unconstitutional was meritless because it was not blatantly overbroad. The failure to give proper notice was fatal to any other challenge to such. Finally, the acts of the employee negatively impacted the work environment at the clerk's office.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1192 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Flax v. DaimlerChrysler Corp.


No. M2005-01768-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 822; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,688


July 12, 2006, Session  
December 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 2007.
Appeal granted by Flax v. DaimlerChrysler Corp., 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 467 (Tenn., May 14, 2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Flax v. DaimlerChrysler Corp., 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 505 (Tenn., July 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 02C-1288. Hamilton V. Gayden, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minivan manufacturer challenged a judgment the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that awarded appellee parents compensatory and punitive damages in their wrongful death action arising from their infant's son's death in automobile accident, alleging claims of defective design, failure to warn, and negligent infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: The parents' son was killed when the minivan he and his mother were riding in was struck by a pickup truck. The infant's head collided with the head of another occupant, whose seat fell backwards during the accident. On appeal of the trial court's judgment for the parents, the court held that the manufacturer waived its defense that the parents' complaint did not contain a valid ad damnum clause under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.08 because it failed to raise the challenge in its answer, instead waiting until four months after the trial concluded. The court held that the evidence was insufficient to support an award to the mother for negligent infliction of emotional distress because she failed to present any expert testimony supporting the claim. Such testimony was required because the mother's claim was a stand-alone claim, as it was for a purely mental injury; she sought no damages for physical injuries or property damage. Even though the trial court erred by instructing the jury on a post-sale duty to warn, as such a duty was not recognized in Tennessee, because the trial court correctly instructed the jury on the parents' remaining theories of recovery, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the parents was reversed as to the mother's negligent infliction of emotional distress claim. The judgment was affirmed as to the jury's wrongful death compensatory award.

Jolly v. Jolly


No. W2005-01845-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 780


September 21, 2006, Session  
December 12, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Jolly v. Jolly, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 422 (Tenn., Apr. 16, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jolly v. Jolly, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1159 (U.S., Jan. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for McNairy County. No. 7471. The Honorable Martha Brasfield, Chancellor.
Jolly v. Jolly, 130 S.W.3d 783, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 251 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband appealed the judgment entered in favor of appellee ex-wife by the Chancery Court, McNairy County (Tennessee) with regard to division of marital property located in Tennessee and credit to the ex-wife for arrearage of child support.


OVERVIEW: A divorce decree was entered in Kansas between the parties. The ex-wife attempted to enforce the Kansas decree in Tennessee with regard to the division of marital property and payment of child support. The ex-husband challenged the constitutionality of several Tennessee statutes, the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act (UIFSA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-2001 et seq., Tennessee's Commission for Uniform Legislation, the UCCJA, and the Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction and Enforcement Act (UCCJEA) and all legislation that proceeded from the National Conference of Commissioner on Uniform State Laws (NCCUSL). The appellate court found that the ex-husband's due process rights were not violated because he was given the opportunity to be heard and was provided proper notice. The Kansas court properly exercised jurisdiction over the ex-husband. Many of the statutes that the ex-husband challenged did not apply to his case. The UIFSA was not vague because it clearly set forth the bases and procedure for establishing jurisdiction over a nonresident. The UIFSA did not violate equal protection because it treated all parents and children who were subject to child custody proceedings equally.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1194 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hood


No. E2005-01061-COA-R3-CD


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


221 S.W.3d 531; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 762


July 17, 2006, Session  
November 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hood, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 257 (Tenn., Mar. 5, 2007)
Related proceeding at In re Hood, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 549 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S49, 555. Jerry Scott, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was adjudicated delinquent in the juvenile court. After a de novo jury trial in the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee), defendant was found to have committed kidnapping and aggravated rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was committed until he reached the age of 19. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erroneously ordered that he be committed for a determinate period of time. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court tried and adjudged defendant delinquent for the offenses of kidnapping and aggravated rape. That was the only "substantial evidence" necessary to justify the trial court's determinate commitment under Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-137. No other justification or consideration was required. In addition, there was evidence that defendant blamed the events on the codefendant and the victim. There was also evidence that defendant showed little remorse for what happened. Thus, there was evidence suggesting that defendant was in need of extensive treatment and rehabilitation. The record did not support defendant's contentions challenging the propriety of the trial court's determinate commitment. The court of appeals also held that a determinate commitment was not more severe than an indefinite commitment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1195 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Eatherly Constr. Co. v. Tenn. Dep't of Labor & Workforce Dev.


No. M2005-00915-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


232 S.W.3d 731; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 763; 21 OSHC (BNA) 1848


May 25, 2006, Session  
November 29, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 03-3314-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee state occupational safety commission found appellant construction company in violation of 29 C.F.R. § 1926.652, an Occupational Safety and Health Administration regulation that prohibited employees from entering a large excavated trench that did not contain adequate protection to prevent the earthen walls from collapsing on employees. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) affirmed the decision. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that its foreman was the only one who entered the unprotected trench and he was not an "employee" as defined by 29 C.F.R. § 1926.32(j) (2006). In the alternative, if a violation had occurred, it was not liable as the foreman's actions constituted employee misconduct. It was undisputed that the deep end of the trench was not properly shorn, sloped, or protected by a trench box as required by 29 C.F.R. § 1926.652(b) or (c) (2006). The company argued that the definition of "employee" in 29 C.F.R. § 1926.32(j) (2006) controlled, as it pertained specifically to the construction industry and was adopted by the commissioner. The appellate court held that although the foreman had supervisory duties, he supervised on behalf of the company and also engaged in the same physical labor as those he supervised, thereby putting him in the same classification as the company's other employees, only with additional supervisory responsibilities. As a consequence, the foreman fell within the definitions of "employee" under, inter alia, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-3-103. The court also found that the company provided scant evidence to support the affirmative defense of employee misconduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the matter was remanded with the costs of the appeal assessed against the construction company.

State v. R.D.S.


No. M2005-00213-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 733


January 11, 2006, Session  
November 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. R.D.S., 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 273 (Tenn., Mar. 12, 2007)
Affirmed by, in part, Remanded by R.D.S. v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 28 (Tenn., Feb. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR04274. R. E. Lee Davies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile high school student, was adjudicated delinquent in the Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) for possession of marijuana and drug paraphernalia. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying the motion to suppress his incriminating statements because he was essentially in custody from the time the deputy and the high school principal approached him and "forced" him to accompany them to his truck, which was in the school's parking lot. The court of appeals disagreed. The deputy testified that she told defendant that she and the principle were going to search his truck and asked him to join them. The deputy informed defendant that the reason for the search was that another student had been found intoxicated and said that he had been in defendant's truck. While defendant argued that the deputy's request was tantamount to an order and that an ordinary student in defendant's situation would not feel free to refuse, neither the language of the request nor its substance demonstrated a degree of compulsion that approximated the deprivation of freedom of movement associated with formal arrest. Defendant was not confined to the principal's office or some other room in the school for the purpose of questioning. Defendant was not in custody for Miranda purposes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Johnson City v. Paduch


No. E2006-00037-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


224 S.W.3d 686; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 732


September 21, 2006, Session  
November 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by City of Johnson City v. Paduch, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 300 (Tenn., Mar. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Washington County. No. 23036. Thomas Seeley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Building owners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Tennessee), which ordered that the owners pay retroactive and prospective fines of $50 per day because of their failure to install a fire control device in a building they constructed as required by a city building code.


OVERVIEW: The building owners constructed a 15,000-square-foot addition and, later, a 5,000-square-foot addition, to a building they co-owned. The city issued the owners a citation for violating a city ordinance by failing to obtain a building permit. Because of the increased size of the building after the additions, the building became subject to requirements for the installation of a fire control device, such as a sprinkler system throughout the building or a fire wall. The circuit court ordered that the owners pay retroactive and prospective fines of $50 dollars per day because of their failure to install a fire control device. On appeal, the owners argued numerous issues, none of which the court deemed to have any merit. For example, the court held that the circuit court did not err by assessing a total of fines in excess of $50 because each fine was a separate offense and did not violate the limitation on fines without a jury under Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14. Moreover, because Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-2-102 pertained to criminal misdemeanors, and this case involved a matter of civil procedure, the owners' argument that the city violated that statute in its prosecution was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Silver Video USA, Inc. v. Summers


No. M2004-00794-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 714


May 5, 2005, Session  
November 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Silver Video USA, Inc. v. Cooper, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 385 (Tenn., Apr. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 03C-3488. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult-oriented businesses appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) holding that the Adult Oriented Establishment Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1401 et seq., was constitutional under Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 19 on the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The Act limited the hours and days during which adult establishments could be open. The businesses sought injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment that Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1402(a) was unconstitutional. On appeal of the trial court's decision holding that the Act was constitutional, the court affirmed. Under intermediate scrutiny, § 7-51-1402(a) was constitutional because: (1) it was not disputed that governments were authorized to enact land use regulations; (2) the Act's restrictions on hours of operation furthered the governmental interest that was unrelated to speech, namely reducing and curtailing the secondary effects of adult-oriented establishments including crime, noise, and traffic congestion; (3) there were many avenues available to disseminate the material and the businesses were open other hours during the day and night, and the material could be purchased after the operating hours of adult-oriented establishments at stores that did not offer predominately sexually-oriented material; and (4) restricting hours of operation was not unduly burdensome. Further, scienter was not a constitutionally required element of an offense under the Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that the Act was constitutional was affirmed.

 

1199 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Metro. Dev. & Hous. Agency v. Eaton


No. M2005-02044-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


216 S.W.3d 327; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 670


June 27, 2006, Session  
October 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Metro. Dev. & Hous. Agency v. Eaton, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 169 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 01C-1109. Walter Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied appellant landowners' motion to alter or amend, Tenn. R. Civ. P. 59.04, after a jury awarded $504,000 as damages for the condemnation of their property. The condemnation action was brought in the context of executing a redevelopment plan drafted by appellee Metropolitan Development and Housing Agency (MDHA) and approved by the Metro Council. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners argued that the trial court abused its discretion by denying the motion and erred in entering the original possession order. The appellate court noted that Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-20-105 restricted MDHA's power with respect to private property in an urban renewal area. The appellate court determined that no proof was offered by the landowners that would satisfy the second element of the Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-20-105 exception to the power of eminent domain. The trial court specifically found that such individual development by the landowners would frustrate the objectives of the urban renewal plan. The landowners could not bring themselves within the exception to eminent domain provided by Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-20-105, and the trial court did not err in granting possession to the MDHA following the possessory hearing of May 24, 2001. Since the Tenn. R. Civ. P. 59 motion filed four years subsequent to the June 25, 2001, order of possession simply sought to relitigate matters that had already been adjudicated, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in overruling the motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McLeay v. Huddleston


No. M2005-02118-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 655; 25 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 425


July 12, 2006, Session  
October 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McLeay v. Huddleston, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 168 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)
Related proceeding at McLeay v. Metro. Hosp. Auth., 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 691 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 03C-123. The Honorable Barbara N. Haynes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the employee, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, her employer and other individuals (employer), in the employee's action after her termination for common law and statutory retaliatory discharge, violations of 42 U.S.C. § 1983, tortuous interference with an employment contract, defamation, and negligence.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated from her position as a physician assistance and she subsequently filed an action against her employer for common law and statutory retaliatory discharge, violations of 42 U.S.C. § 1983, tortuous interference with an employment contract, defamation, and negligence after her termination. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the employer and the court affirmed on appeal. The record did not support the employee's claims under the Tennessee Public Protection Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-1-304, because the record reflected that she was terminated for violating hospital protocols and policies. The employee admitted that she initiated a surgery consent form by partially completing the form. Her claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was also inappropriate because there was no evidence that the employer had any policies, customs, or practices that were in violation of the employee's First Amendment rights. Her defamation claim was without merit because she failed to establish the publication element and failed to establish that she suffered any injury as a result of the defamatory statements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
